  <td colspan="1" align="left">
    <div>that contravention</div>

  </td>
</tr></table><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Item 2&#151;_director_ includes a shadow director

(see section 9).

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>A person who acquires securities as a result of an offer that was

accompanied by a profile statement is taken to have acquired the securities in

reliance on both the profile statement and the prospectus for the offer.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>An action under subsection (1) may begin at any time within 6 years after the day on which the cause of action arose.</dd> <dt>(4)</dt><dd>This Part does not affect any liability that a person has under any other law. </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Conduct that contravenes subsection 728(1) is expressly

excluded from the operation of section 995.

 </dl></dl>

730  People liable on disclosure document to inform person making the offer about deficiencies in the disclosure document

<dl compact="">

		A person referred to in the table in section 729 must notify the person

making the offer in writing as soon as practicable if they become aware during

the application period that:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a material statement in the disclosure document is misleading or

deceptive; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>there is a material omission from the disclosure document of material

required by section 710, 711, 712, 713, 714 or 715; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>a material new circumstance that:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>has arisen since the disclosure document was lodged; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>would have been required by section 710, 711, 712, 713, 714 or 715 to be

included in the disclosure document if it had arisen before the disclosure

document was lodged.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

731  Due diligence defence for prospectuses

_Reasonable inquiries and reasonable beliefstatements_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A person does not commit an offence against subsection 728(3), and is not

liable under section 729 for a contravention of subsection 728(1), because of a

misleading or deceptive statement in a prospectus if the person proves that

they:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>made all inquiries (if any) that were reasonable in the circumstances;

<center>Back to Top</center>

and

</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>after doing so, believed on reasonable grounds that the statement was not

misleading or deceptive.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Reasonable inquiries and reasonable beliefomissions_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>A person does not commit an offence against subsection 728(3), and is not

liable under section 729 for a contravention of subsection 728(1), because of

an omission from a prospectus in relation to a particular matter if the person

proves that they:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>made all inquiries (if any) that were reasonable in the circumstances;

and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>after doing so, believed on reasonable grounds that there was no omission

from the prospectus in relation to that matter.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

732  Lack of knowledge defence for offer information statements and profile statements

_Not knowing statement misleading or deceptive_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A person does not commit an offence against subsection 728(3), and is not

liable under section 729 for a contravention of subsection 728(1), because of a

misleading or deceptive statement in an offer information statement or profile

statement if the person proves that they did not know that the statement was

misleading or deceptive.

</dd> </dl>

_Not knowing there was an omission_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>A person does not commit an offence against subsection 728(3), and is not

liable under section 729 for a contravention of subsection 728(1), because of

an omission from an offer information statement or profile statement in

relation to a particular matter if the person proves that they did not know

that there was an omission from the statement in relation to that matter.

</dd> </dl>

733  General defences for all disclosure documents

_Reasonable reliance on information given by someone elsestatements and omissions_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A person does not commit an offence against subsection 728(3), and is not

liable under section 729 for a contravention against subsection 728(1), because

of a misleading or deceptive statement in, or an omission from, a disclosure

document if the person proves that they placed reasonable reliance on

information given to them by:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>if the person is a body&#151;someone other than a director, employee or agent

of the body; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>if the person is an individual&#151;someone other than an employee or agent of

the individual.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>For the purposes of subsection (1), a person is not the agent of a body or

individual merely because they perform a particular professional or advisory

function for the body or individual.

</dd> </dl>

_Withdrawal of consentstatements and omissions_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>A person who is named in a disclosure document as:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>being a proposed director or underwriter; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>making a statement included in the document; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>making a statement on the basis of which a statement is included in the

document;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

does not commit an offence against subsection 728(3), and is not liable under section 729 for a contravention against subsection 728(1), because of a misleading or deceptive statement in, or an omission from, a disclosure document if the person proves that they publicly withdrew their consent to being named in the document in that way.

_Unawareness of new matter_

<dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>A person does not commit an offence against subsection 728(3), and is not

liable under section 729 for a contravention of subsection 728(1), because of a

new circumstance that has arisen since the disclosure document was lodged if

the person proves that they were not aware of the matter.

</dd> 

</dl>

734  Restrictions on advertising and publicity

_No advertising or publicity for offers covered by the exception for 20 issues in 12 months_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A person must not:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>advertise; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>publish a statement that directly or indirectly refers to;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

an offer, or intended offer, of securities that would need a disclosure document but for subsection 708(1) (exception for 20 issues in 12 months).

_Advertising or publicity for offers that need a disclosure document_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>If an offer, or intended offer, of securities needs a disclosure document,

a person must not:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>advertise the offer or intended offer; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>publish a statement that:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>directly or indirectly refers to the offer or intended offer; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>is reasonably likely to induce people to apply for the securities;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

unless the advertisement or publication is authorised by subsection (4), (5), (6) or (7).

_Image advertising_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>In deciding whether a statement:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>indirectly refers to an offer, or intended offer, of securities; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>is reasonably likely to induce people to apply for securities;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

have regard to whether the statement:

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>forms part of the normal advertising of a body's products or services and

is genuinely directed at maintaining its existing customers, or attracting new

customers, for those products or services; and</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>communicates information that materially deals with the affairs of the

body; and</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>is likely to encourage investment decisions being made on the basis of the

statement rather than on the basis of information contained in a disclosure

document.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Dissemination of disclosure document_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>A person may disseminate a disclosure document that has been lodged with

ASIC without contravening subsection (2). This does not apply if an order under

section 739 is in force in relation to the offer.

</dd> </dl>

_Advertising and publicity before the disclosure document is lodged_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>Before the disclosure document is lodged, an advertisement or publication

does not contravene subsection (2) if it:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>if the offer is of securities in a class already quoted&#151;includes a

statement that:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>a disclosure document for the offer will be made available when the

securities are offered; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>anyone who wishes to acquire the securities will need to complete the

application form that will be in or will accompany the disclosure document; and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>in any other case&#151;contains the following but nothing more:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>a statement that identifies the offeror and the securities</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>a statement that a disclosure document for the offer will be made

available when the securities are offered</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>a statement that anyone who wants to acquire the securities will need to

complete the application form that will be in or will accompany the disclosure

document</dd>

<dt>(iv)</dt><dd>a statement of how to arrange to receive a copy of the disclosure

document.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

To satisfy paragraph (b), the advertisement or publication must include all of the statements referred to in subparagraphs (i), (ii) and (iii). It may include the statement referred to in subparagraph (iv).

_Advertising and publicity after the disclosure document is lodged_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(6)</dt><dd>After the disclosure document is lodged, an advertisement or publication

does not contravene subsection (2) if it includes a statement that:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the offers of the securities will be made in, or accompanied by, a copy of

the disclosure document; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>anyone wishing to acquire the securities will need to complete the

application form that will be in or will accompany the disclosure document.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_General exceptions_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(7)</dt><dd>An advertisement or publication does not contravene subsection (2) if it:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>relates to an offer of securities of a listed body and consists of a

notice or report by the body, or one of its officers, about its affairs to the

relevant securities exchange; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>consists solely of a notice or report of a general meeting of the body;

or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>consists solely of a report about the body that is published by the body

and:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>does not contain information that materially affects affairs of the body

other than information previously made available in a disclosure document that

has been lodged, an annual report or a report referred to in paragraph (a) or

(b); and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>does not refer (whether directly or indirectly) to the offer; or

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>is a news report or is genuine comment, in a newspaper or periodical or on

radio or television relating to:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>a disclosure document that has been lodged or information contained in

such a disclosure document; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>a notice or report covered by paragraph (a), (b) or (c); or

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>is a report about the securities of a body or proposed body published by

someone who is not:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the body; or </dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>acting at the instigation of, or by arrangement with, the body; or</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>a director of the body; or</dd>

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dt>(iv)</dt><dd>a person who has an interest in the success of the issue or sale of the

securities.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

Paragraphs (d) and (e) do not apply if anyone gives consideration or another benefit for publishing the report.

_Liability of publishers_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(8)</dt><dd>A person does not contravene subsection (1) or (2) by publishing an

advertisement or statement if they publish it in the ordinary course of a

business of:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>publishing a newspaper or magazine; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>broadcasting by radio or television;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

and the person did not know and had no reason to suspect that its publication would amount to a contravention of a provision of this Chapter.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Depending on the circumstances of the publication, the

person may, however, commit an offence by being involved in someone else's

contravention of subsection (1) or (2).

 </dl></dl>

_Pathfinder documents_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(9)</dt><dd>A person does not contravene subsection (1) or (2) by sending a draft

disclosure document for securities to a person if an offer of the securities to

the person would not require a disclosure document because of subsection 708(8)

or (10) (sophisticated investors) or 708(11) (professional investors).

</dd> </dl>

735  Obligation to keep consents and other documents

<dl compact="">

		A person who offers securities under a disclosure document must keep a

consent required in respect of the document by subsection 716(2) or section 720.

 </dl>

736  Securities hawking prohibited

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A person must not offer securities for issue or sale in the course of, or

because of, an unsolicited:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>meeting with another person; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>telephone call to another person;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

unless the offer is exempted under subsection (2).

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Section 700 extends offers to include invitations and

distributing application forms.

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>Subsection (1) does not prohibit an offer of securities if:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the offer does not need a disclosure document because of subsection 708(8)

or (10) (sophisticated investors); or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the offer does not need a disclosure document because of subsection

708(11) (professional investors); or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the offer is an offer of listed securities made by telephone by a licensed

securities dealer; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>the offer is made to a client by a licensed securities dealer through whom

the client has bought or sold securities in the last 12 months.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

Division 2&#151;Remedies
 737  Remedies for investors

_Right to withdraw and have money returned_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>If securities are issued to a person in contravention of section 724

(situation calling for a supplementary or replacement document), the person has

the right to return the securities and to have their application money repaid.

This is so even if the company that issued the securities is being wound up.</dd> 
<center>Back to Top</center>
 <dt>(2)</dt><dd>A right referred to in subsection (1) is exercisable by written notice given to the company within 1 month after the date of the issue.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>If the body or the seller does not repay the money as required by subsection (1), the directors of the body or seller are personally liable to repay the money. </dd> 

</dl>

738  Securities may be returned and refund obtained

<dl compact="">

		If securities are issued or transferred to a person as a result of an offer

that contravenes section 736, the person may return the securities within 1

month after the issue or transfer. If they do so, they are entitled to be

repaid the amount they paid for the securities.

 </dl>

Part 6D.4&#151;ASIC's powers

739  ASIC stop orders

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>If ASIC is satisfied that an offer of securities under a disclosure

document lodged with ASIC would contravene section 728, ASIC may order that no

offers, issues, sales or transfers of the securities be made while the order is

in force.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>Before making an order under subsection (1), ASIC must: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>hold a hearing; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>give a reasonable opportunity to any interested people to make oral or

written submissions to ASIC on whether an order should be made.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>If ASIC considers that any delay in making an order under subsection (1)

pending the holding of a hearing would be prejudicial to the public interest,

ASIC may make an interim order that no offers, issues, sales or transfers of

the securities be made while the interim order is in force. The interim order

may be made without holding a hearing and lasts for 21 days after the day on

which it is made unless revoked before then.</dd> <dt>(4)</dt><dd>At any time during the hearing, ASIC may make an interim order that no offers, issues, sales or transfers of the securities be made while the interim order is in force. The interim order lasts until: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>ASIC makes an order under subsection (1) after the conclusion of the

hearing; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the interim order is revoked;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

whichever happens first.

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>An order under subsection (1), (3) or (4) must be in writing and must be

served on the person who is ordered not to offer, issue, sell or transfer

securities under the disclosure document.

</dd> </dl>

740  Anti-avoidance determinations

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>ASIC may determine in writing that a number of different bodies are

closely related and that their transactions should be aggregated for the

purposes of this Chapter. If ASIC does so:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>an issue, sale or transfer of securities in any other bodies is taken to

also be an issue, sale or transfer of the securities of each of the other

bodies by those bodies; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>any money received from an issue, sale or transfer of securities in any of

the bodies is taken to also be received by each of the other bodies from an

issue, sale or transfer of its own securities.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

ASIC must give written notice of the determination to each of the bodies.

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>ASIC may determine in writing that the transactions of a body and of a

person who controls the body should be aggregated for the purposes of this

Chapter. If ASIC does so:

</dd> 
<center>Back to Top</center>

</dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>an issue of securities in the body is taken to also be the transfer of the

securities by the controller; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>any money received from an issue of securities in the body is taken to

also be received by the controller from a transfer of the securities; and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>a sale or transfer of securities in the body by the controller is taken to

also be the issue of the securities by the body; and</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>any money received from a sale or transfer of securities in the body by

the controller is taken to also be received by the body from an issue of the

securities.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

ASIC must give written notice of the determination to the body and the controller.

741  ASIC's power to exempt and modify

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>ASIC may:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>exempt a person from a provision of this Chapter; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>declare that this Chapter applies to a person as if specified provisions

were omitted, modified or varied as specified in the declaration.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The exemption or declaration may do all or any of the following:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>apply to all or specified provisions of this Chapter</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>apply to all persons, specified persons, or a specified class of persons</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>relate to all securities, specified securities or a specified class of

securities</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>relate to any other matter generally or as specified.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>An exemption may apply unconditionally or subject to specified conditions.

A person to whom a condition specified in an exemption applies must comply with

the condition. The Court may order the person to comply with the condition in a

specified way _._ Only ASIC may apply to the Court for the order.</dd> <dt>(4)</dt><dd>The exemption or declaration must be in writing and ASIC must publish notice of it in the _Gazette_.</dd> <dt>(5)</dt><dd>For the purposes of this section, the _provisions of this Chapter_ include: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>regulations made for the purposes of this Chapter; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>definitions in this Law or the regulations as they apply to references in:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>this Chapter; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>regulations made for the purposes of this Chapter; and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>Division 12 of Part 11.2.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

6  Part 9.4B

Repeal the Part, substitute:

Part 9.4B&#151;Civil consequences of contravening civil penalty provisions

1317E  Declarations of contravention

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>If a Court is satisfied that a person has contravened 1 of the following

provisions, it must make a declaration of contravention:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>subsections 180(1) and 181(1) and (2), 182(1) and (2), 183(1) and (2)

(officers' duties)</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>subsection 209(2)(related parties rules)</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>subsections 254L(2), 256D(3), 259F(2) and 260D(2) (share capital

<center>Back to Top</center>

transactions)

</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>subsection 344(1) (requirements for financial reports)</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>subsection 588G(2) (insolvent trading)</dd>

<dt>(f)</dt><dd>subsection 601FC(1)</dd>

<dt>(g)</dt><dd>subsection 601FD(1)</dd>

<dt>(h)</dt><dd>subsection 601FE(1)</dd>

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>section 601FG</dd>

<dt>(j)</dt><dd>subsection 601JD(1).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

These provisions are the _civil penalty provisions_.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Once a declaration has been made ASIC can then seek a

pecuniary penalty order (section 1317G) or a disqualification order (section

206C).

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>A declaration of contravention must specify the following:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the Court that made the declaration</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the civil penalty provision that was contravened</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the person who contravened the provision</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>the conduct that constituted the contravention</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>the corporation or registered scheme to which the conduct related.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

1317F  Declaration of contravention is conclusive evidence

<dl compact="">

		A declaration of contravention is conclusive evidence of the matters referred

to in subsection 1317E(2).

 </dl>

1317G  Pecuniary penalty orders

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A Court may order a person to pay the Commonwealth a pecuniary penalty of

up to $200,000 if:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a declaration of contravention by the person has been made under section

1317E; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the contravention:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>materially prejudices the interests of the corporation or scheme, or its

members; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>materially prejudices the corporation's ability to pay its creditors;

or</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>is serious.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The penalty is a civil debt payable to ASIC on the Commonwealth's behalf.

ASIC or the Commonwealth may enforce the order as if it were an order made in

civil proceedings against the person to recover a debt due by the person. The

debt arising from the order is taken to be a judgment debt.

</dd> </dl>

1317H  Compensation orders

_Compensation for damage suffered_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A Court may order a person to compensate a corporation or registered

scheme for damage suffered by the corporation or scheme if:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the person has contravened a civil penalty provision in relation to the

corporation or scheme; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the damage resulted from the contravention.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

The order must specify the amount of the compensation.

<dl compact="">

		_Damage includes profits_ <dt>(2)</dt><dd>In determining the damage suffered by the corporation or scheme for the purposes of making a compensation order, include profits made by any person 
<center>Back to Top</center>
 resulting from the contravention or the offence. 

</dd> </dl>

_Damage includes diminution of value of scheme property_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>In determining the damage suffered by the scheme for the purposes of

making a compensation order, include any diminution in the value of the

property of the scheme.</dd> <dt>(4)</dt><dd>If the responsible entity for a registered scheme is ordered to compensate the scheme, the responsible entity must transfer the amount of the compensation to scheme property. If anyone else is ordered to compensate the scheme, the responsible entity may recover the compensation on behalf of the scheme.</dd> 		_Recovery of damage_ <dt>(5)</dt><dd>A compensation order may be enforced as if it were a judgment of the Court. </dd> </dl>

1317J  Who may apply for a declaration or order

_Application by ASIC_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>ASIC may apply for a declaration of contravention, a pecuniary penalty

order or a compensation order.

</dd> </dl>

_Application by corporation_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The corporation, or the responsible entity for the registered scheme, may

apply for a compensation order.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>The corporation, or the responsible entity for the registered scheme, may intervene in an application for a declaration of contravention or a pecuniary penalty order in relation to the corporation or scheme. The corporation or responsible entity is entitled to be heard on all matters other than whether the declaration or order should be made. </dd> </dl>

_No one else may apply_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>No person may apply for a declaration of contravention, a pecuniary

penalty order or a compensation order unless permitted by this section.</dd> <dt>(5)</dt><dd>Subsection (4) does not exclude the operation of the _Director of Public Prosecutions Act 1983_ or that Act as applying as a law of this jurisdiction. </dd> </dl>

1317K  Time limit for application for a declaration or order

<dl compact="">

		Proceedings for a declaration of contravention, a pecuniary penalty order, or

a compensation order, may be started no later than 6 years after the

contravention.

 </dl>

1317L  Civil evidence and procedure rules for declarations of contravention and civil penalty orders

<dl compact="">

		The Court must apply the rules of evidence and procedure for civil matters

when hearing proceedings for:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a declaration of contravention; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a pecuniary penalty order.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

1317M  Civil proceedings after criminal proceedings

<dl compact="">

		A court must not make a declaration of contravention or a pecuniary penalty

order against a person for a contravention if the person has been convicted of

an offence constituted by conduct that is substantially the same as the conduct

constituting the contravention.

 </dl>

1317N  Criminal proceedings during civil proceedings

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>Proceedings for a declaration of contravention or pecuniary penalty order

against a person are stayed if:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>criminal proceedings are started or have already been started against the

person for an offence; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the offence is constituted by conduct that is substantially the same as

the conduct alleged to  constitute the contravention.

<center>Back to Top</center>

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The proceedings for the declaration or order may be resumed if the person

is not convicted of the offence. Otherwise, the proceedings for the declaration

or order are dismissed.

</dd> </dl>

1317P  Criminal proceedings after civil proceedings

<dl compact="">

		Criminal proceedings may be started against a person for conduct that is

substantially the same as conduct constituting a contravention of a civil

penalty provision regardless of whether:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a declaration of contravention has been made against the person; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a pecuniary penalty order has been made against the person; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>a compensation order has been made against the person; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>the person has been disqualified from managing a corporation under Part

2D.6.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

1317Q  Evidence given in proceedings for penalty not admissible in criminal proceedings

<dl compact="">

		Evidence of information given or evidence of production of documents by an

individual is not admissible in criminal proceedings against the individual if:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the individual previously gave the evidence or produced the documents in

proceedings for a pecuniary penalty order against the individual for a

contravention of a civil penalty provision (whether or not the order was made);

and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the conduct alleged to constitute the offence is substantially the same as

the conduct that was claimed to constitute the contravention.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

However, this does not apply to a criminal proceeding in respect of the falsity of the evidence given by the individual in the proceedings for the pecuniary penalty order.

1317R  ASIC requiring person to assist

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>ASIC may require a person to give all reasonable assistance in connection

with:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>an application for a declaration of contravention or a pecuniary penalty

order; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>criminal proceedings for an offence against this Law.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>ASIC can require the person to assist in connection with an application

for a declaration or order if, and only if:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>it appears to ASIC that someone other than the person required to assist

may have contravened a civil penalty provision; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>ASIC suspects or believes that the person required to assist can give

information relevant to the application.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>ASIC can require the person to assist in connection with criminal

proceedings if, and only if:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>it appears to ASIC that the person required to assist is unlikely to be a

defendant in the proceedings; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the person required to assist is, in relation to a person who is or should

be a defendant in the proceedings:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>an employee or agent (including a banker or auditor) of the other person;

<center>Back to Top</center>

or

</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>if the other person is a corporation&#151;an officer of the other person;

or</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>if the other person is an individual&#151;a partner of the other person.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>ASIC can require the person to assist regardless of whether:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>an application for the declaration or penalty order has actually been

made; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>criminal proceedings for the offence have actually begun.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>The person cannot be required to assist if they are or have been a lawyer

for:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>in an application for a declaration or penalty order&#151;the person suspected

of the contravention; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>in criminal proceedings&#151;a defendant or likely defendant in the

proceedings.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(6)</dt><dd>The requirement to assist must be given in writing.</dd> <dt>(7)</dt><dd>The Court may order the person to comply with the requirement in a specified way. Only ASIC may apply to the Court for an order under this subsection _._ </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	The person must comply with the requirement and may commit

an offence if they do not, even if there is no order under this subsection (see

section 104 and subsection 1311(1)).

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(8)</dt><dd>This section does not limit and is not limited by section 49 of the ASC

Law.

</dd> </dl>

1317S  Relief from liability for contravention of civil penalty provision 

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>In this section:

</dd> </dl>

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_eligible proceedings_:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>means proceedings for a contravention of a civil penalty provision

(including proceedings under section 588M, 588W or 1317H of the Corporations

Law of this jurisdiction); and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>does not include proceedings for an offence (except so far as the

proceedings relate to the question whether the court should make an order under

section 588K or 1317H of that Law).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>If:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>eligible proceedings are brought against a person; and</dd>

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>in the proceedings it appears to the court that the person has, or may

have, contravened a civil penalty provision but that:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the person has acted honestly; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>having regard to all the circumstances of the case (including, where

applicable, those connected with the person's appointment as an officer of a

corporation or of a Part 5.7 body), the person ought fairly to be excused for

<center>Back to Top</center>

the contravention;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

the court may relieve the person either wholly or partly from a liability to which the person would otherwise be subject, or that might otherwise be imposed on the person, because of the contravention.

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>In determining under subsection (2) whether a person ought fairly to be

excused for a contravention of section 588G, the matters to which regard is to

be had include, but are not limited to:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>any action the person took with a view to appointing an administrator of

the company or Part 5.7 body; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>when that action was taken; and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the results of that action.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>If a person thinks that eligible proceedings will or may be begun against

them, they may apply to the Court for relief.</dd> <dt>(5)</dt><dd>On an application under subsection (4), the Court may grant relief under subsection (2) as if the eligible proceedings had been begun in the Court.</dd> <dt>(6)</dt><dd>For the purposes of subsection (2) as applying for the purposes of a case tried by a judge with a jury: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a reference in that subsection to the court is a reference to the judge;

and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the relief that may be granted includes withdrawing the case in whole or

in part from the jury and directing judgment to be entered for the defendant on

such terms as to costs as the judge thinks appropriate.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(7)</dt><dd>Nothing in this section limits, or is limited by, section 1318.

</dd> </dl>

7  After section 1325

Insert:

1325A  Orders if contravention of Chapter 6, 6A, 6B or 6C

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The Court may make any order or orders (including a remedial order) that

it considers appropriate if a person:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>contravenes a provision of Chapter 6, 6A, 6B or 6C; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>contravenes a condition on a consent given by ASIC under section 652B;

or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>states in a notice under section 672B about securities that they do not

know particular information about:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the securities; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>someone who has a relevant interest in, or has given instructions in

relation to, the securities.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note 1:	Section 9 defines _remedial order_. Note 2:	Sections 659B and 659C deal with court proceedings during and after a takeover bid.  </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The Court may make any order or orders (including a remedial order) that

it considers appropriate if:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the consideration offered under a takeover bid is or includes securities;

and</dd>

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the offers under the bid or the bidder's statement states or implies that

the securities are to be quoted on a stock market of a securities exchange

(whether in Australia or elsewhere) and:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>an application for admission to quotation is not made within 7 days after

the start of the bid period; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>permission for admission to quotation is not granted within 7 days after

the end of the bid period.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Section 9 defines _remedial order_.

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>An order under this section may be made on application by the following:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>ASIC</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the company, or the responsible entity of the registered scheme, whose

securities are involved in the contravention</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>a member or former member of that company or scheme</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>a person from whom the relevant interest in the securities were acquired</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>a person whose interests are affected by the contravention.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

1325B  Court may order bidder to make offers

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>If a bidder making a takeover bid for a class of securities contravenes

section 631 by failing to make offers under the bid within time and ASIC

applies for an order under this section, the Court may:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>order the bidder to send, to each holder of securities in that class, an

offer to which the bidder's statement relates within a specified time; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>make any ancillary orders it thinks appropriate including orders that the

bidder:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>send notices setting out specified information with the offer; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>send copies of the notice within a specified period to the target and, if

the target is listed, to the relevant securities exchange; and</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>lodge a copy of the notice with ASIC within a specified period.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>Offers sent in accordance with an order under this section are taken to be

made under a takeover bid.

</dd> </dl>

1325C  Unfair or unconscionable agreements, payments or benefits

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The Court may make orders under subsection (2) if:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a body corporate gives, or enters into an agreement to give, a director or

secretary of the body corporate or a related body corporate a benefit

(including a payment or an agreement to employ them, or engage their services,

for a fixed period); and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the agreement is entered into or the benefit is given:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>within 12 months after the start of the bid period for a takeover bid for

the securities of the body corporate or a related body corporate; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>at a time when the directors of the body corporate have reason to believe

that a takeover bid is to be made in respect of securities of the body

corporate or a related body corporate; and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the Court is satisfied that the agreement or benefit was unfair or

unconscionable having regard to the interests of the body corporate.

</dd>

<center>Back to Top</center>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The Court may:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>declare the agreement, or any part of it, to be void or to have always

been void; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>direct a person to whom a benefit is given, or another specified person,

to:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>make a payment or transfer property to the body corporate; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>do any other act for the benefit of the body corporate; or

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>make any other order it considers appropriate.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>This section does not apply to an agreement or benefit that has been

approved by an ordinary resolution of the body corporate (whether before or

after the agreement was entered into or the benefit given) with no vote being

cast by the person who is to receive the benefit or their associates.</dd> <dt>(4)</dt><dd>An order under this section may be made on application by: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the body corporate; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>ASIC; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>members who together hold shares carrying at least 10% of the votes

attached to voting shares in the body corporate or a related body corporate;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

within 12 months, or any longer period that the Court thinks appropriate in the circumstances, after the agreement is entered into or the benefit given.

1325D  Contravention due to inadvertence etc.

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The Court may declare that any act, document or matter:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>is not invalid merely because a person has contravened a provision of

Chapter 6, 6A, 6B or 6C; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>has had effect at all times as if there had been no contravention;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

if the Court is satisfied that the contravention ought to be excused in all the circumstances.

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>An application for an order under subsection (1) may be made by any

interested person.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>If the Court is satisfied that in all the circumstances a contravention of a provision of Chapter 6, 6A, 6B or 6C ought to be excused, the Court must not make an order under section 1325A, 1325B or 1325C other than: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>an order restraining the exercise of voting or other rights attached to

securities; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>an order that an exercise of voting or other rights attached to securities

be disregarded.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>In determining whether or not a contravention of a provision by a person

ought to be excused, have regard to the contravention being caused by any of

the following:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the person's inadvertence or mistake</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the person not having been aware of a relevant fact or occurrence </dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>circumstances beyond the control of the person. 

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>This section applies notwithstanding anything contained in any other

<center>Back to Top</center>

provision of this Chapter.

</dd> </dl>

1325E  Orders to secure compliance

<dl compact="">

		In order to secure compliance with an order under section 1325A, 1325B or

1325C, the Court may direct a person to:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>do a specified act; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>refrain from doing a specified act.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

8  After Division 11 of Part 11.2

Insert:

Division 12&#151;Changes resulting from the Corporate Law Economic Reform Program Act 1999
 1466  Meaning of commencement, new Law and old Law

<dl compact="">

		In this Division:

 </dl>

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_commencement_ means the commencement of Schedule 1 to the

_Corporate Law Economic Reform Program Act 1999_. _new Law_ means this Law as in force after commencement. _old Law_ means this Law as in force immediately before commencement.  </dl></dl>

1467  General&#151;references to provisions of old Law in laws and other documents

in any document, to a provision of the old Law is to be read after commencement

as a reference to the corresponding provision of the new Law except so far as

the contrary intention appears in the law or document.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>Without limiting subsection (1), the following table sets out provisions of the old Law that correspond to particular provisions of the new Law: </dd> </dl>

  </td>
  <td colspan="1" align="left">
    <div>before the commencement of section 206A of the new Law, a person had permission under a previous corresponding law to section 206F or 206G to manage a corporation</div>

  </td>
  <td colspan="1" align="left">
    <div>Part 2D.6 applies as if the person had permission to manage the corporation under section 206F or 206G.</div>

  </td>
</tr>
<tr align="left">
  <td colspan="1" align="left">
    <div>21</div>

  </td>
  <td colspan="1" align="left">
    <div>before the commencement of section 203D of the new Law, a company gives notice of intention under a corresponding previous provision to subsection 203D(2)</div>

  </td>
  <td colspan="1" align="left">
    <div>section 203D applies as if the notice had been given under subsection 203D(2).</div>

  </td>
</tr></table>1470  Related party transactions&#151;continued application of old Law

<dl compact="">

		Chapter 2E  of the old Law continues to apply to the giving of a

financial benefit (within the meaning of the old law) if:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the benefit was given before commencement; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>some or all materials required to be lodged with ASIC in relation to the

benefit by section 243U of the old Law were lodged with ASIC before

commencement; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the benefit is given under a contract made before commencement.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

1471  Oppressive conduct of affairs&#151;applications made before commencement

<dl compact="">

		If an application was made under section 246AA of the old Law and not finally

determined before the commencement of section 232 of the new Law, then section

246AA of the old Law continues to apply in respect of the application.

<center>Back to Top</center>

</dl>

1472  Proceedings on behalf of a company&#151;intervention in proceedings started before commencement

<dl compact="">

		Under Part 2F.1A (sections 236 to 242) of the new Law, a person may apply for

leave to intervene, and intervene, in proceedings started before commencement.

 </dl>

1473  Civil penalty provisions&#151;application of new Law

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>Part 9.4B of the old Law continues to apply in relation to:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a contravention of a civil penalty provision listed in section 1317DA of

the old Law; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>an offence committed against one of those civil penalty provisions;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

despite its repeal.

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>Part 9.4B of the new Law applies in relation to a contravention of a civil

penalty provision listed in section 1317E of the new law.

</dd> </dl>

1474  Civil penalty orders made under old Law

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An order in force under paragraph 1317EA(3)(a) of the old Law immediately

before commencement continues to have effect after commencement as if it were

made under section 206C of the new Law.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>An order in force under paragraph 1317EA(3)(b) of the old Law immediately before commencement continues to have effect after commencement as if it were made under section 1317G of the new Law.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>An order in force under section 1317HA or 1317HB of the old Law immediately before commencement continues to have effect after commencement as if it were made under section 1317H of the new Law. </dd> </dl>

1475  Fundraising&#151;general application

_General rule (new law applies to offers made after commencement)_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>Except as provided for in subsection (2), this Chapter applies to offers

of securities made after the commencement of this Chapter.

</dd> </dl>

_Prospectus, or section 1043C or 1043D notice, lodged before commencement covered by old law_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>If a prospectus, or a notice under section 1043C or 1043D, is lodged with

ASIC before commencement, the old Law continues to apply to:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the prospectus or notice; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>offers made under the prospectus or notice; and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the issue or transfer of securities as a result of the offer.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

1476  Fundraising&#151;application of new section 712

<dl compact="">

		Section 712 of the new Law (incorporation by reference of documents lodged

with ASIC) applies to documents lodged with ASIC before commencement.

 </dl>

1477  Fundraising&#151;registration of managed investment schemes

<dl compact="">

		Subsection 601ED(2) of the new Law applies as if issues of interests that:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>were made before commencement; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>were excluded issues under the old Law (disregarding paragraph 66(2)(da)

of that Law);

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

were issued that did not need disclosure to investors under section 706 of the new Law.

</dd>
