<dl compact="">

		An obligation under Part 6.7 or 6.8 of the old Law continues after

commencement as if that Part had not been repealed if the period for complying

with the obligation has commenced but not ended before commencement.

 </dl>

1489  Takeovers&#151;ASIC power to pass on information obtained under the old Law

<dl compact="">

		Section 672C of the new Law applies to information obtained under Part 6.8 of

the old Law as if it had been obtained in response to a direction under section

672A of the new Law.

 </dl>

1490  Takeovers&#151;application of section 111AG of the new Law

<dl compact="">

		Section 111AG of the new Law applies after commencement as if a takeover

scheme as defined in section 603 of the old Law or a corresponding previous law

were an off-market takeover bid.

 </dl>

1491  Compulsory acquisitions&#151;application of Part 6A.5 of the new Law

<dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

		Part 6A.5 of the new Law (sections 668A and 668B) applies to consideration

paid before commencement.

</dl>

1492  Compulsory acquisitions&#151;unclaimed moneys

<dl compact="">

		If, immediately before commencement, a company holds property in trust for a

person under subsection 701(11) of the old Law, the company must continue to

hold the property in trust for the person in accordance with subsection 666B(2)

of the new Law.

 </dl>

1493  Accounting standards&#151;standards in force before commencement

<dl compact="">

		For the avoidance of doubt, an accounting standard that was in force under

section 334 immediately before commencement continues in force after that

commencement as if it had been made by the AASB under that section immediately

after that commencement.

 </dl>

<center>**

###  CORPORATE LAW ECONOMIC REFORM PROGRAM ACT 1999Schedule 2&#151;Main amendments of the Australian Securities and Investments Commission Act 1989 
**</center>

 1  Part 12

Repeal the Part, substitute:

Part 12&#151;Accounting standards

224  Main objects of this Part

<dl compact="">

		The main objects of this Part are:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>to facilitate the development of accounting standards that require the

provision of financial information that:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>allows users to make and evaluate decisions about allocating scarce

resources; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>assists directors to discharge their obligations in relation to financial

reporting; and</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>is relevant to assessing performance, financial position, financing and

investment; and</dd>

<dt>(iv)</dt><dd>is relevant and reliable; and</dd>

<dt>(v)</dt><dd>facilitates comparability; and</dd>

<dt>(vi)</dt><dd>is readily understandable; and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>to facilitate the Australian economy by:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>reducing the cost of capital; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>enabling Australian entities to compete effectively overseas; and</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>having accounting standards that are clearly stated and easy to

understand; and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>to maintain investor confidence in the Australian economy (including its

capital markets).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

Division 1&#151;The Australian financial reporting system
 225  Establishment, functions and powers of the Financial Reporting Council

_Establishment_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A Financial Reporting Council is established.

</dd> </dl>

_Functions_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The FRC functions are:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>to provide broad oversight of the process for setting accounting standards

in Australia and to give the Minister reports and advice on that process; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>to appoint the members of the AASB (other than the Chair); and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>to approve and monitor the AASB's:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>priorities; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>business plan; and</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>budget; and</dd>

<dt>(iv)</dt><dd>staffing arrangements (including level, structure and composition of

staffing); and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>to determine the AASB's broad strategic direction; and</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>to give the AASB directions, advice or feedback on matters of general

policy and the AASB's procedures; and</dd>

<dt>(f)</dt><dd>to monitor the development of international accounting standards and the

accounting standards that apply in major international financial centres, and:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>to further the development of a single set of accounting standards for

world-wide use with appropriate regard to international developments; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>to promote the adoption of international best practice accounting

standards in the Australian accounting standard setting process if doing so

would be in the best interests of both the private and public sectors in the

Australian economy; and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(g)</dt><dd>to monitor:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the operation of accounting standards to assess their continued relevance

and their effectiveness in achieving their objectives in respect of both the

private and public sectors of the Australian economy; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>the effectiveness of the AASB's consultative arrangements; and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(h)</dt><dd>to seek contributions towards the costs of the Australian accounting

standard setting process; and</dd>

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>to monitor and periodically review the level of funding, and the funding

arrangements, for the AASB; and</dd>

<dt>(j)</dt><dd>to establish appropriate consultative mechanisms; and</dd>

<dt>(k)</dt><dd>to advance and promote the main objects of this Part; and</dd>

<dt>(l)</dt><dd>any other functions that the Minister confers on the FRC by written notice

to the FRC Chairman.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Powers_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>As well as any other powers conferred by this Act, the FRC has power to do

all things necessary or convenient to be done for or in connection with the

performance of its functions.</dd> <dt>(4)</dt><dd>Without limiting subsection (3), the FRC may establish committees and advisory groups. </dd> </dl>

_Restriction on powers_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>The FRC does not have power to direct the AASB in relation to the

development, or making, of a particular standard.</dd> <dt>(6)</dt><dd>The FRC does not have power to veto a standard formulated and recommended by the AASB. </dd> </dl>

226  Establishment of the Australian Accounting Standards Board

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An Australian Accounting Standards Board is established.

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Subsection 236B(3) specifies the qualifications needed for

appointment to the Board.

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The AASB:

</dd> 

</dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>is a body corporate with perpetual succession; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>must have a common seal; and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>may acquire, hold and dispose of real and personal property; and</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>may sue and be sued in its corporate name.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	The _Commonwealth Authorities and Companies Act 1997_

applies to the AASB. This Act makes provision for reporting obligations (annual

report, interim reports and estimates), accounting records, audit, banking,

investment of funds and duties of officers.

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>All courts, judges and persons acting judicially must:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>take judicial notice of the imprint of the common seal of the AASB

appearing on a document; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>presume that the document was duly sealed.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

227  AASB's functions and powers

_Functions_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The functions of the AASB are:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>to develop a conceptual framework, not having the force of an accounting

standard, for the purpose of evaluating proposed accounting standards and

international standards; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>to make accounting standards under section 334 of the Corporations Law for

the purposes of the national scheme laws; and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>to formulate accounting standards for other purposes; and</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>to participate in and contribute to the development of a single set of

accounting standards for world-wide use; and</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>to advance and promote the main objects of this Part.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note 1:	The standards made under paragraph (b) are given legal

effect by the Corporations Law. The standards formulated under paragraph (c) do

not have legal effect under the Corporations Law itself but may be applied or

adopted by some other authority. Note 2:	See section 224 and sections 228 to 233 for the framework within which the AASB is to formulate and make accounting standards.  </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>In carrying out its functions under paragraphs (1)(a) and (d), the AASB

must have regard to the interests of Australian corporations which raise or

propose to raise capital in major international financial centres.

</dd> </dl>

_Powers_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>The AASB has power to:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>engage staff and consultants; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>establish committees, advisory panels and consultative groups; and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>receive money contributed towards its operating costs; and</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>do anything else that is necessary for, or reasonably incidental to, the

performance of its functions.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Manner of making and formulating standards_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>Without limiting paragraph (1)(b) or (c), the AASB may make or formulate

an accounting standard by issuing the text of an international accounting

standard. The text of the international accounting standard may be modified to

the extent necessary to take account of the Australian legal or institutional

environment and, in particular, to ensure that any disclosure and transparency

<center>Back to Top</center>

provisions in the standard are appropriate to the Australian legal or

institutional environment.

</dd> </dl>

_Manner of participating in the development of international standards_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>Without limiting paragraph (1)(d), the AASB may distribute the text of a

draft international accounting standard (whether or not modified to take

account of the Australian legal or institutional environment) for the purposes

of consultation.

</dd> </dl>

_Constitutional basis_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(6)</dt><dd>This Part confers functions and powers to the extent to which they are not

in excess of the legislative power of the Commonwealth.</dd> <dt>(7)</dt><dd>Without limiting subsection (6), this Part confers functions and powers to the extent to which doing so promotes, encourages and facilitates the integration and efficiency of, and investment in, Australia's national economy. </dd> </dl>

Division 2&#151;Accounting standards
 228  Purposive interpretation of standards

_Objects of this Part_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>In interpreting an accounting standard made or formulated by the AASB, a

construction that would promote the objects of this Part is to be preferred to

a construction that would not promote those objects.

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Section 224 states the main objects of this Part.

 </dl></dl>

_Purposes or objects of particular standard_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>In interpreting an accounting standard made or formulated by the AASB, a

construction that would promote a purpose or object of the standard (to the

extent to which it is not inconsistent with the objects of this Part) is to be

preferred to a construction that would not promote that purpose or object. This

is so even if the purpose or object is not expressly stated in the standard.

</dd> </dl>

229  Generic and specific standards

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>Accounting standards made or formulated by the AASB may:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>be of general or limited application (including a limitation to specified

bodies or undertakings); and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>differ according to differences in time, place or circumstance.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>In making and formulating accounting standards, the AASB:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>must have regard to the suitability of a proposed standard for different

types of entities; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>may apply different accounting requirements to different types of

entities; and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>must ensure that there are appropriate accounting standards for each type

of entity that must comply with accounting standards.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

230  Comparative amounts

<dl compact="">

		The accounting standards for the preparation of financial reports for a

period may require the inclusion in those reports of comparative amounts for

earlier periods.

 </dl>

231  Cost/benefit analysis

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The AASB must carry out a cost/benefit analysis of the impact of a

proposed accounting standard before making or formulating the standard. This

does not apply where the standard is being made or formulated by issuing the

<center>Back to Top</center>

text of an international standard (whether or not modified to take account of

the Australian legal or institutional environment).

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Subsection 227(3) allows the AASB to make or formulate a

standard by issuing the text of an international standard. Under subsection (2)

of this section, the AASB will have done a cost/benefit analysis of the

international standard used in that way.

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The AASB must carry out a cost/benefit analysis of the impact of a

proposed international accounting standard before:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>providing comments on a draft of the standard; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>proposing the standard for adoption as an international standard.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>The AASB has to comply with subsections (1) and (2) only to the extent to

which it is reasonably practicable to do so in the circumstances.</dd> <dt>(4)</dt><dd>The Minister may direct the AASB to give the Minister details of a cost/benefit analysis carried out under this section. The AASB must comply with the direction. </dd> </dl>

232  FRC views

<dl compact="">

		In performing its functions, the AASB must:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>follow the broad strategic direction determined by the FRC under paragraph

225(2)(d); and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>follow the general policy directions given by the FRC under paragraph

225(2)(e); and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>take into account the advice and feedback on matters of general policy

given by the FRC under paragraph 225(2)(e).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

233  International accounting standards

<dl compact="">

		The Minister may give the AASB a direction about the role of international

accounting standards in the Australian accounting standard setting system.

Before giving a direction under this section, the Minister must receive and

consider a report from the FRC about the desirability of giving the direction.

The AASB must comply with the direction.

 </dl>

234  Validity of accounting standards

<dl compact="">

		A failure to comply with this Division in relation to the making of an

accounting standard does not affect the validity of the standard.

 </dl>

Division 3&#151;Administrative provisions
 Subdivision A&#151;The Financial Reporting Council
 235A  Membership of FRC

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The members of the Council are appointed by the Minister in writing. The

Minister may appoint a person by specifying an organisation or body that is to

choose the person who is appointed.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>The members hold office on the terms and conditions that are determined by the Minister.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>The Minister must appoint one of the members to be Chairman of the Council. The appointment must be in writing. The Council may appoint one of its members to be Deputy Chairman of the Council. </dd> </dl>

235B  Annual report

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>As soon as practicable after 30 June in each year, and in any event before

31 October, the FRC must give the Minister a report on:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the operations of:

<center>Back to Top</center>

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the FRC and its committees and advisory groups; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>the AASB and its committees, advisory panels and consultative groups; and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the achievement of the objects set out in section 224;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

during the year that ended on 30 June in that year.

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The report must include details of any change to the AASB's priorities or

business plan that was made as a result of action taken by the FRC.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>The Minister may grant an extension of time in special circumstances.</dd> <dt>(4)</dt><dd>The Minister must table the report in each House of the Parliament as soon as practicable.</dd> <dt>(5)</dt><dd>If the FRC is established during the last 3 months of a year ending on 30 June: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the FRC is not required to prepare an annual report for that year; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the period from the time of establishment to the end of that year must be

dealt with in the next annual report.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(6)</dt><dd>If the FRC is established during the first 9 months of a year ending on 30

June, the annual report for that year must cover the period from the time of

establishment to the end of that year.

</dd> </dl>

235C  Procedure

<dl compact="">

		The FRC may determine its own procedural rules (including rules as to notice

of meetings, quorum and voting).

 </dl>

Subdivision B&#151;The Australian Accounting Standards Board
 236A  Procedure

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>Meetings of the AASB are to be chaired by:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the Chair; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the Deputy Chair if the Chair is absent; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>a member chosen by the members present if both the Chair and the Deputy

Chair are absent.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>If a meeting of the AASB, or a part of one of its meetings, concerns the

contents of accounting standards or international accounting standards, the

meeting or that part of it must be held in public.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>The AASB must: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>comply with any directions about its procedure that the FRC gives under

paragraph 225(2)(e); and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>take into account the advice and feedback about its procedure that the FRC

gives under paragraph 225(2)(e).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>Otherwise, the AASB may determine its own procedural rules (including

rules as to notice of meetings, quorum and voting).

</dd> </dl>

236B  Appointment of members of the AASB

_Appointment of Chair_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The Minister appoints the Chair of the AASB.

</dd> </dl>

_Appointment of other members_

<dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The FRC appoints the other members of the AASB. The AASB may appoint one

of its members to be Deputy Chair of the AASB.

</dd> 

</dl>

_Qualification for appointment_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>A person must not be appointed as a member of the AASB unless their

knowledge of, or experience in, business, accounting, law or government

qualifies them for the appointment.

</dd> </dl>

_Appointment document_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>An appointment under subsection (1) or (2) is to be made in writing.

</dd> </dl>

_Period of appointment_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>The appointment document must specify the period of the appointment (not

exceeding 5 years). A member holds office for the period specified in the

appointment document and is eligible for reappointment.

</dd> </dl>

_Terms and conditions of appointment_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(6)</dt><dd>The Chair holds office on the terms and conditions that are determined by

the Minister. The other members hold office on the terms and conditions

determined by the FRC.

</dd> </dl>

236C  Resignation and termination of appointment

_Resignation_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A member of the AASB may resign their appointment by giving a written

resignation to:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>if the member is the Chair of the AASB&#151;the Minister; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>in any other case&#151;the Chair of the FRC.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Termination of Chair&apos;s appointment_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The Chair is not to be removed from office except as provided by

subsection (3) or (4).</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>The Minister may terminate the appointment of the Chair of the AASB for: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>misbehaviour or physical or mental incapacity; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>breach of the terms and conditions of their appointment.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>The Minister must terminate the appointment of the Chair of the AASB if

the Chair:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>becomes bankrupt; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>applies to take the benefit of any law for the relief of bankrupt or

insolvent debtors; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>compounds with their creditors; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>makes an assignment of their remuneration or property for the benefit of

their creditors; or</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>contravenes section 237.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Termination of ordinary member&apos;s appointment_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>A member of the AASB (other than the Chair) is not to be removed from

office except as provided by subsection (6) or (7).</dd> <dt>(6)</dt><dd>The FRC may terminate the appointment of a member of the AASB (other than the Chair) for: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>misbehaviour or physical or mental incapacity; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>breach of the terms and conditions of the member's appointment.

<center>Back to Top</center>

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(7)</dt><dd>The FRC must terminate the appointment of a member of the AASB (other than

the Chair) if the member:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>becomes bankrupt; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>applies to take the benefit of any law for the relief of bankrupt or

insolvent debtors; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>compounds with their creditors; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>makes an assignment of their remuneration or property for the benefit of

their creditors; or</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>contravenes section 237.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

236D  Acting appointments

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The Minister may appoint a person to act as Chair of the AASB:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>during a vacancy in the office of Chair (whether or not an appointment has

previously been made to the office); or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>during any period, or during all periods, when the Chair is absent from

duty or from Australia, or is for any reason unable to perform the duties of

the office.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The AASB may appoint one of its members to act as Deputy Chair of the AASB:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>during a vacancy in the office of Deputy Chair (whether or not an

appointment has previously been made to the office); or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>during any period, or during all periods, when the Deputy Chair is absent

from duty or from Australia, or is for any reason unable to perform the duties

of the office.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>The FRC may appoint a person to act as a member of the AASB (other than

the Chair):

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>during a vacancy in the office of member (whether or not an appointment

has previously been made to the office); or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>during any period, or during all periods, when the member is absent from

duty or from Australia, or is for any reason unable to perform the duties of

the office.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>Anything done by or in relation to a person purporting to act under an

appointment is not invalid merely because:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the occasion for the appointment had not arisen; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>there was a defect in connection with the appointment; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the appointment had ceased to have effect; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>the occasion to act had not arisen or had ceased.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

Subdivision C&#151;Confidentiality
 237  Confidentiality

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The FRC and the AASB must take all reasonable measures to protect from

unauthorised use or disclosure information given to it in confidence.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>For the purposes of subsection (1), the disclosure of information is taken to be authorised if the disclosure: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>is required or permitted by a law of the Commonwealth or a prescribed law

of this or any other jurisdiction; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>is made in order to enable an authority or person in a country outside

<center>Back to Top</center>

Australia and the external Territories to perform or exercise a function or

power that corresponds, or is analogous, to any of the FRC's or the AASB's

functions or powers; or

</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>is made to a body that sets international accounting standards; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>is made to ASIC for the purposes of its performance of its functions under

national scheme laws.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

Subdivision D&#151;Financial matters
 238  Application of money

<dl compact="">

		The money of the AASB must be applied only:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>in payment or discharge of the costs, expenses and other obligations

incurred by the AASB in the performance of its functions or the exercise of its

powers under this Act; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>in meeting the administrative expenses of the FRC and the committees and

advisory groups it establishes; and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>in payment of any remuneration and allowances payable to any person

appointed under this Part.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

</dd>

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

Insert:

 </dl></dl>

70  After section 1324

Insert:

1324A  Provisions relating to prosecutions

<dl compact="">

		In the prosecution of a person for an offence in respect of a contravention

of a provision of Chapter 5C or 6D or Part 7.11, the Court may do either or

both of the following:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>grant an injunction under section 1324 against the person in relation to:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the conduct that constitutes, or is alleged to constitute, the offence;

or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>other conduct of that kind

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>make an order under section 1324B in respect of the person.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

1324B  Order to disclose information or publish advertisements

<dl compact="">

		Without limiting section 1324, if, on the application of ASIC, the Court is

satisfied that a person has engaged in conduct constituting a contravention of

a provision of Chapter 5C or 6D or Part 7.11, the Court may make either or both

of the following orders against that person or a person involved in the

contravention:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>an order requiring the person to whom it is directed to disclose, in the

manner specified in the order, to:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the public; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>a particular person; or</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>a particular class of persons;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		the information, or information of a kind, that is specified in the order and

is in the person's possession or to which the person has access

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>an order requiring the person to whom it is directed to publish, at the

person's own expense, in the manner and at times specified in the order,

advertisements whose terms are specified in, or are to be determined in

accordance with, the order.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

Part 2&#151;Amendments relating to new Chapter 2L (Debentures)
 76  Section 9 (definition of borrowing corporation)

Repeal the definition.

77  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_borrower_, in relation to a debenture, means the

body that is or will be liable to repay money under the debenture.

 </dl></dl>

78  Section 9 (definition of debenture)

Repeal the definition, substitute:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_debenture_ of a body means a chose in action that includes an

undertaking by the body to repay as a debt money deposited with or lent to the

body. The chose in action may (but need not) include a charge over property of

the body to secure repayment of the money. However, a debenture does not

include:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>an undertaking to repay money deposited with or lent to the body by a

person if:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the person deposits or lends the money in the ordinary course of a

business carried on by the person; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>the body receives the money in the ordinary course of carrying on a

business that neither comprises nor forms part of a business of borrowing money

and providing finance

</dd>

<center>Back to Top</center>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>an undertaking by an Australian ADI to repay money deposited with it, or

lent to it, in the ordinary course of its banking business</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>an undertaking to pay money under:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>a cheque; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>an order for the payment of money; or</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>a bill of exchange

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>an undertaking to pay money under a promissory note that has a face value

of at least $50,000</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>an undertaking by a body corporate to pay money to a related body

corporate</dd>

<dt>(f)</dt><dd>an undertaking to repay money that is prescribed by the regulations.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

For the purposes of this definition, if a chose in action that includes an

undertaking by a body to pay money as a debt is offered as consideration for

the acquisition of securities under an off-market takeover bid, or is issued

under a compromise or arrangement under Part 5.1, the undertaking is taken to

be an undertaking to repay as a debt money deposited with or lent to the body.

 </dl></dl>

79  Section 9 (definition of eligible money market dealer)

Omit "paragraph 65(1)(a)", substitute "section 65".

80  Section 9 (definition of excluded corporation)

Repeal the definition.

81  Section 9 (definition of exempt securities)

Repeal the definition.

82  Section 9 (definition of guarantor body)

Repeal the definition.

83  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_guarantor_, in relation to a debenture, means a body that has

guaranteed, or has agreed to guarantee, the repayment of any money deposited or

lent to the borrower under the debenture.

 </dl></dl>

84  Section 65

Repeal the section, substitute:

65  Eligible money market dealer

<dl compact="">

		ASIC may declare a body corporate to be an authorised dealer in the short

term money market by notice published in the _Gazette_.

 </dl>

85  Paragraph 111AH(1)(a)

Omit "1047", substitute "601CZB".

111AI  Debentures that need trustee appointed under section 260FA

requires the borrower to appoint a trustee.

 </dl>

</dd>

Add:

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>For the purposes of this Division, a foreign company carries on business

in this jurisdiction if it:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>offers debentures in this jurisdiction; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>is a guarantor body for debentures offered in this jurisdiction;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

and Part 2L.1 applies to the debentures.

101  After Division 3 of Part 5B.2

Insert:

Division 4&#151;Register of debenture holders for non-companies
 601CZA  Certain documents are debentures

<dl compact="">

		For the purposes of this Division, choses in action (including an

undertaking) that fall into one of the exceptions in paragraphs (a), (b), (e)

and (f) of the definition of _debenture_ in section 9 must also be

entered into the register of debenture holders.

 </dl>

601CZB  Register of debenture holders to be maintained by non-companies

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A body that is not a company must set up and maintain a register of

debenture holders if it issues debentures covered by Chapter 2L.

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note 1:	Companies have to keep a register of debenture holders

under sections 168 and 171\. Note 2:	The register may be kept on computer (see section 1306).  </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The register must contain the following information about each debenture

holder:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>their name and address</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the amount of the debentures held.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>A body's failure to comply with this section in relation to a debenture

does not affect the debenture itself.

</dd> 
<center>Back to Top</center>

</dl>

601CZC  Location of register

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The register must be kept at:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the body's registered office; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the body's principal place of business in Australia; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>a place in Australia (whether of the body or of someone else) where the

work involved in maintaining the register is done; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>another place approved by ASIC.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The body must lodge with ASIC a notice of the address at which the

register is kept within 7 days after the register is:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>established at an office that is neither the body's registered office nor

at its principal place of business; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>moved from one office to another.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

Notice is not required for moving the register between the registered office and an office at the principal place of business.

601CZD  Application of sections 173 to 177

<dl compact="">

		Sections 173 to 177 apply to a register kept under this Division as if it

were kept under Chapter 2C.

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Sections 173 to 177 deal with rights to inspect the

register and get copies, the obligations of agents who maintain the register,

correction of the register, the evidential value of the register and the use of

information on the register.

 </dl></dl>

102  After section 563A

Insert:

563AAA  Redemption of debentures

_Priorities_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>Debentures of a company under a trust deed that are issued in place of

debentures under that deed that have been redeemed have the priority that the

redeemed debentures would have had if they had never been redeemed.

</dd> </dl>

_Deposit of debentures to secure advance_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>Debentures of a company are not to be taken to be redeemed merely because:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the debentures secure advances on current account or otherwise; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the company's account ceases to be in debit while those debentures remain

available.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

103  Subsection 1302(1)

Omit "or 1047".

109  Section 9 (definition of director)

Repeal the definition, substitute:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_director_ of a company or other body means:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a person who:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>is appointed to the position of a director; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>is appointed to the position of an alternate director and is acting in

that capacity;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		regardless of the name that is given to their position; and

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>unless the contrary intention appears, a person who is not validly

appointed as a director if:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>they act in the position of a director; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>the directors of the company or body are accustomed to act in accordance

with the person's instructions or wishes.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

Subparagraph (b)(ii) does not apply merely because the directors act on advice given by the person in the proper performance of functions attaching to the person's professional capacity, or the person's business relationship with the directors or the company or body.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Paragraph (b)&#151;Contrary intention&#151;Examples of provisions

for which a person referred to in paragraph (b) would not be included in the

term "director" are:

 </dl></dl>

*	section 249C (power to call meetings of a company's members)
 *	subsection 251A(3) (signing minutes of meetings)
 *	section 205B (notice to ASIC of change of address).

112  Section 9 (definition of officer)

Repeal the definition, substitute:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

_officer_ of a corporation means:

</dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a director or secretary of the corporation; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a person:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>who makes, or participates in making, decisions that affect the whole, or

a substantial part, of the business of the corporation; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>who has the capacity to affect significantly the corporation's financial

standing; or</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>in accordance with whose instructions or wishes the directors of the

corporation are accustomed to act (excluding advice given by the person in the

proper performance of functions attaching to the person's professional capacity

or their business relationship with the directors or the corporation); or

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>a receiver, or receiver and manager, of the property of the corporation;

or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>an administrator of the corporation; or</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>an administrator of a deed of company arrangement executed by the

corporation; or</dd>

<dt>(f)</dt><dd>a liquidator of the corporation; or</dd>

<dt>(g)</dt><dd>a trustee or other person administering a compromise or arrangement made

between the corporation and someone else.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Section 201B contains rules about who is a director of a

corporation.

 </dl></dl>

187  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_remuneration_ of an officer or employee of a corporation. A

benefit given to an officer or employee of a corporation is

_remuneration_ if and only if the benefit, were it received by a

director of the corporation, would be remuneration of the director for the

purposes of an accounting standard that deals with disclosure in companies'

financial reports of information about related parties. For the purposes of

this definition, the following are not officers of a corporation:

<center>Back to Top</center>

</dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a receiver, or receiver and manager, of the property of the corporation</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>an administrator of the corporation</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>an administrator of a deed of company arrangement executed by the

corporation</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>a liquidator of the corporation</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>a trustee or other person administering a compromise or arrangement made

between the corporation and someone else.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

188  Section 9 (definition of sibling entity)

189  After section 50

Insert in Division 6 of Part 1.2:

50AA  Control

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>For the purposes of this Law, an entity controls a second entity if the

first entity has the capacity to determine the outcome of decisions about the

second entity's financial and operating policies.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>In determining whether the first entity has this capacity: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the practical influence the first entity can exert (rather than the rights

it can enforce) is the issue to be considered; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>any practice or pattern of behaviour affecting the second entity's

financial or operating policies is to be taken into account (even if it

involves a breach of an agreement or a breach of trust).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>The first entity does not control the second entity merely because the

first entity and a third entity jointly have the capacity to determine the

outcome of decisions about the second entity's financial and operating

policies.</dd> <dt>(4)</dt><dd>If the first entity: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>has the capacity to influence decisions about the second entity's

financial and operating policies; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>is under a legal obligation to exercise that capacity for the benefit of

someone other than the first entity's members;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

the first entity is taken not to control the second entity.

Omit "243H, 243ZE", substitute "208, 209".

Repeal the subsection.

193  Section 601LA

194  Sections 601LB to 601LE

Repeal the sections, substitute:

601LB  Replacement section 207

<dl compact="">

		Chapter 2E applies as if section 207 were replaced by the following section:

 </dl>

207  Purpose

<dl compact="">

		The rules in this Chapter, as they apply to a registered scheme, are designed

to protect the interests of the scheme's members as a whole, by requiring

member approval for giving financial benefits to the responsible entity or its

related parties that come out of scheme property or that could endanger those

interests.

 </dl>

601LC  Replacement section 208

<dl compact="">

		Chapter 2E applies as if section 208 were replaced by the following section:

 </dl>

208  Need for member approval for financial benefit

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>If all the following conditions are satisfied in relation to a financial

<center>Back to Top</center>

benefit:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the benefit is given by:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the responsible entity of a registered scheme; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>an entity that the responsible entity controls; or</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>an agent of, or person engaged by, the responsible entity

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the benefit either:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>is given out of the scheme property; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>could endanger the scheme property

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the benefit is given to:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the person or a related party; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>another person referred to in paragraph (a) or a related party of that

person;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

then, for the person referred to in paragraph (a) to give the benefit, 
 either:

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>the person referred to in paragraph (a) must:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>obtain the approval of the scheme's members in the way set out in sections

217 to 227; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>give the benefit within 15 months after the approval; or

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>the giving of the benefit must fall within an exception set out in

sections 210 to 216.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Section 228 defines _related party_, section

191 defines _entity_, section 191 defines

_control_ and section 229 affects the meaning of _giving a financial benefit_.

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>If:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the giving of the benefit is required by a contract; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the making of the contract was approved in accordance with subparagraph

(1)(d)(i) as a financial benefit given to the entity or related party; and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the contract was made:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>within 15 months after that approval; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>before that approval, if the contract was conditional on the approval

being obtained;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

member approval for the giving of the benefit is taken to have been given and the benefit need not be given within the 15 months.

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>Subsection (1) does not prevent the responsible entity from paying itself

fees, and exercising rights to an indemnity, as provided for in the scheme's

constitution under subsection 601GA(2).

</dd> 
<center>Back to Top</center>

</dl>

601LD  Omission of sections 213, 214 and 224

<dl compact="">

		Chapter 2E applies as if sections 213, 214 and 224 were omitted.

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Instead of section 224, the rule in section 253E will apply.

 </dl></dl>

601LE  Modification of section 225

<dl compact="">

		Chapter 2E applies as if subsection 225(1) were amended by omitting

"subsection 224(1)" and substituting "section 253E".

 </dl>

257  Section 9 (definition of associate)

Repeal the definition, substitute:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_associate_: The following are the associates of a bidder making a

takeover offer, a substantial holder or a 90% holder:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>if the bidder or holder is a body corporate:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>a body corporate it controls; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>a body corporate that controls it; or</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>a body corporate that is controlled by an entity that controls it

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a person with whom the bidder or holder has, or proposes to enter into, a

relevant agreement for the purpose of controlling or influencing the

composition of the body's board or the conduct of the body's affairs</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>a person with whom the bidder or holder is acting, or proposes to act, in

concert in relation to the body's affairs.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

Otherwise a person's associates are determined under sections 10 to 17.

258  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

_bid class_ of securities for a takeover bid is the class of

securities to which the securities being bid for belong.

</dl></dl>

259  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_bidder_ for a takeover bid means the person who makes or proposes

to make, or each of the people who make or propose to make, the offers under

the bid (whether personally or by an agent or nominee).

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	The dealer who announces a market bid is not the bidder;

the bidder is the person or people on whose behalf the announcement is made.

 </dl></dl>

260  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

and 637 as supplemented.

 </dl></dl>

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_bid period_:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>for an off-market bid&#151;starts when the bidder's statement is given to the

target and ends:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>1 month later if no offers are made under the bid; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>at the end of the offer period; and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>for a market bid&#151;starts when the bid is announced to the relevant

securities exchange and ends at the end of the offer period.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

</dd>

269  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_convertible securities_: Securities are convertible into another

class of securities if the holder may have the other class of securities issued

to them by the exercise of rights attached to those securities. An option may

be a convertible security even if it is non-renounceable.

 </dl></dl>

270  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_current market bid price_ for securities covered by a market bid

is the price specified in the announcement of the bid as increased or decreased

during the offer period.

 </dl></dl>

271  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_date_ of a takeover bid is:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>for an off-market bid&#151;the date on which offers are first made under the

bid; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>for a market bid&#151;the date on which the bid is announced to the relevant

securities exchange.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

272  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_defeating condition_ for a takeover bid means a condition that:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>will, in circumstances referred to in the condition, result in the

rescission of, or entitle the bidder to rescind, a takeover contract; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>prevents a binding takeover contract from resulting from an acceptance of

the offer unless or until the condition is fulfilled.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

273  Section 9 (definition of dispose of)

Repeal the definition, substitute:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_dispose_ of a futures contract has the meaning given by sections

24, 26, 27 and 28\. For the purposes of Chapter 6, a person who has a relevant

interest in securities _disposes_ of the securities if, and only

if, they cease to have a relevant interest in the securities.

 </dl></dl>

274  Section 9 (definition of enter into)

Repeal the definition, substitute:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_enter into_: A person who:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>enters into, or becomes a party to, a relevant agreement in relation to

voting shares or other securities; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>exercises an option to have voting shares or other securities issued or

granted;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

is taken to enter into a transaction in relation to the shares or securities. _Enter into_, in relation to a futures contract, has a meaning affected by subsection 72(2).

275  Section 9 (paragraph (a) of the definition of Exchange subsidiary)

Repeal the paragraph.

276  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

exchange to be an exchange traded option.

</dl></dl>

277  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_foreign holder_ of securities means a holder of the securities

whose address, as shown in the register in which details of their holding is

recorded, is a place outside Australia and the external Territories.

 </dl></dl>

278  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_highest outside purchase price_ for a takeover bid is the highest

amount paid or payable by the bidder for a security in the bid class under a

purchase made outside the bid and during the bid period.

 </dl></dl>

279  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_listed_: A company, managed investment scheme or other body is

listed if it is included in the official list of a securities exchange.

 </dl></dl>

280  Section 9 (definition of listing rules)

Repeal the definition, substitute:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_listing rules_, when used in Chapter 7, has the meaning given by

section 761.

 </dl></dl>

281  Section 9 (definition of make)

Repeal the definition.

282  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_market bid_ means a takeover bid made under Chapter 6 as a market

bid (see section 616).

 </dl></dl>

283  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_necessary transfer documents_ for the transfer of securities to a

person means the documents that are sufficient to enable the person to become

the holder of the securities.

 </dl></dl>

284  Section 9 (definition of offer)

Repeal the definition.

285  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

under the bid remain open.

 </dl></dl>

286  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_off-market bid_ means a takeover bid made under Chapter 6 as an

off-market bid (see section 616).

 </dl></dl>

287  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_on-market_: a transaction of any kind is an

_on-market_ transaction if it is effected on a stock market of a

securities exchange and is:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>an on-market transaction as defined in the rules governing the operation

of the exchange; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>if those rules do not define on-market transactions&#151;effected in the

ordinary course of trading on the stock market.

<center>Back to Top</center>

</dd>

288  Section 9

company.

 </dl></dl>

289  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_proportional takeover bid_ means an off-market bid for a specified

proportion of the securities in the bid class (see paragraph 618(1)(b)).

 </dl></dl>

293  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_remedial order_ means an order that:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>restrains a person from exercising any voting or other rights attached to

securities</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>directs a body corporate not to make or to defer payment of an amount due

from the body corporate in respect of securities</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>restrains a person from acquiring securities or an interest in

securities</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>directs a person to dispose of, or not to dispose of, securities or

interests in securities</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>directs the disposal referred to in paragraph (d):

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>to be made within a specified time; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>to be made subject to specified conditions; or</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>not to be made to a specified person or persons or to a specified class

or classes of persons

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(f)</dt><dd>directs a specified person to pay to the body corporate an amount equal to

<center>Back to Top</center>

any profit or benefit that the person obtains because of the disposal referred

to in paragraph (d)

</dd>

<dt>(g)</dt><dd>vests securities, or an interest in securities, in ASIC</dd>

<dt>(h)</dt><dd>directs a body corporate not to register the transfer or transmission of

securities</dd>

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>cancels securities issued as consideration for offers under a takeover

bid</dd>

<dt>(j)</dt><dd>declares that an exercise of the voting or other rights attached to

securities be disregarded</dd>

<dt>(k)</dt><dd>cancels or declares voidable:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>an agreement or offer relating to a takeover bid, or a proposed takeover

bid; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>any other agreement or offer in connection with the acquisition of

securities or relevant interests in securities

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(l)</dt><dd>directs a person to give specified information to the holders of

securities of a body corporate</dd>

<dt>(m)</dt><dd>directs a body corporate not to issue securities to a person</dd>

<dt>(n)</dt><dd>if an order of a kind referred to in paragraphs (a) to (m) is in force in

respect of securities&#151;directs the registered holder of the securities to give

written notice of the order to any person whom the holder knows to be entitled

to exercise a right to vote attached to those securities</dd>

<dt>(o)</dt><dd>directs a body corporate to repeal or modify its existing constitution or

adopt a particular constitution</dd>

<dt>(p)</dt><dd>if a person has failed to comply with a requirement of Chapter 6, 6A, 6B

or 6C __ directs that person to comply with that requirement.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

294  Section 9

295  Section 9 (definition of stock market)

296  Section 9

Insert:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_substantial holding_: A person has a substantial holding in a body

corporate, or listed registered managed investment scheme, if:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the total votes attached to voting shares in the body, or voting interests

in the scheme, in which they or their associates:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>have relevant interests; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>would have a relevant interest but for subsection 609(6) (exchange traded

options) or 609(7) (conditional agreements);

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		is 5% or more of the total number of votes attached to voting shares in the

body, or interests in the scheme; or

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the person has made a takeover bid for voting shares in the body, or

voting interests in the scheme, and the takeover period has started and not yet

ended.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	For _relevant interest_, see section 608.

 </dl></dl>

 </dl></dl>

306  Section 9 (definition of voting share)

Repeal the definition, substitute:

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_voting share_ in a body corporate means an issued share in the

body that carries any voting rights beyond the following:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a right to vote while a dividend (or part of a dividend) in respect of the

share is unpaid</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a right to vote on a proposal to reduce the body's share capital</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>a right to vote on a resolution to approve the terms of a buy-back

agreement</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>a right to vote on a proposal that affects the rights attached to the

share</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>a right to vote on a proposal to wind the body up</dd>

<dt>(f)</dt><dd>a right to vote on a proposal for the disposal of the whole of the body's

property, business and undertaking</dd>

<dt>(g)</dt><dd>a right to vote during the body's winding up.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

 </dl></dl>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>has been in any way, by act or omission, directly or indirectly, knowingly

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>has conspired with others to effect the contravention.
