10  At the end of section 6

Add:

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>A maximum penalty that is specified:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>at the foot of a clause of a Schedule to this Act (other than a clause

that is divided into subclauses); or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>at the foot of a subclause of a Schedule to this Act;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

indicates that a person who contravenes the clause or subclause is guilty of an offence against the clause or subclause that is punishable, on conviction, by a penalty up to that maximum.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note 1:	Chapter 2 of the _Criminal Code_ sets out the

general principles of criminal responsibility. Note 2:	If the specified penalty is imprisonment only, section 4B of the _Crimes Act 1914_ allows the court to impose a fine instead of imprisonment or in addition to imprisonment.  </dl></dl>

11  Division 4 of Part 3

Repeal the Division, substitute:

Division 4&#151;Conduct of officers
 21  Background to duties of directors, other officers and employees

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>This Part sets out some of the most significant duties of officers and

employees of Commonwealth authorities. Other duties are imposed by other

provisions of this Act and other laws (including the general law).</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>Section 5 defines both _director_ and _officer_._Officer_ includes, as well as directors, other people who are concerned in, or take part in, the management of the authority. </dd> </dl>

Subdivision A&#151;General duties
 22  Care and diligence&#151;civil obligation only

_Care and diligenceofficers_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An officer of a Commonwealth authority must exercise his or her powers and

discharge his or her duties with the degree of care and diligence that a

reasonable person would exercise if he or she:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>were an officer of a Commonwealth authority in the Commonwealth

authority's circumstances; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>occupied the office held by, and had the same responsibilities within the

Commonwealth authority as, the officer.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	This subsection is a civil penalty provision (see Schedule

2).

 </dl></dl>

_Business judgment rule_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>An officer of a Commonwealth authority who makes a business judgment is

taken to meet the requirements of subsection (1), and their equivalent duties

at common law and in equity, in respect of the judgment if he or she:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>makes the judgment in good faith for a proper purpose; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>does not have a material personal interest in the subject matter of the

judgment; and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>informs himself or herself about the subject matter of the judgment to the

extent he or she reasonably believes to be appropriate; and</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>rationally believes that the judgment is in the best interests of the

Commonwealth authority.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

The officer's belief that the judgment is in the best interests of the Commonwealth authority is a rational one unless the belief is one that no reasonable person in his or her position would hold.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	This subsection only operates in relation to duties under

this section and their equivalents at common law or in equity (including the

duty of care that arises under the common law principles governing liability

for negligence)&#151;it does not operate in relation to duties under any other

provision of this Act or under any other laws.

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>In this section:

</dd> 

</dl>

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_business judgment_ means any decision to take or not take action

in respect of a matter relevant to the operations of the Commonwealth authority.

 </dl></dl>

23  Good faith&#151;civil obligations

_Good faithofficers_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An officer of a Commonwealth authority must exercise his or her powers and

discharge his or her duties:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>in good faith in the best interests of the Commonwealth authority; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>for a proper purpose.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note 1:	This subsection is a civil penalty provision (see

Schedule 2). Note 2:	Section 187 of the Corporations Law deals with the position of directors of wholly-owned subsidiaries of Commonwealth authorities.  </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>A person who is involved in a contravention of subsection (1) contravenes

this subsection.

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note 1:	Section 5 defines _involved_. Note 2:	This subsection is a civil penalty provision (see Schedule 2).  </dl></dl>

24  Use of position&#151;civil obligations

_Use of positionofficers and employees_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An officer or employee of a Commonwealth authority must not improperly use

his or her position to:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>gain an advantage for him or her or someone else; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>cause detriment to the Commonwealth authority or to another person.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note 1:	Section 27A makes provision for officers who are also

public servants. Note 2:	This subsection is a civil penalty provision (see Schedule 2).  </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>A person who is involved in a contravention of subsection (1) contravenes

this subsection.

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note 1:	Section 5 defines _involved_. Note 2:	This subsection is a civil penalty provision (see Schedule 2).  </dl></dl>

25  Use of information&#151;civil obligations

_Use of informationofficers and employees_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A person who obtains information because they are, or have been, an

officer or employee of a Commonwealth authority must not improperly use the

information to:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>gain an advantage for himself or herself or someone else; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>cause detriment to the Commonwealth authority or to another person.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note 1:	Section 27A makes provision for officers who are also

<center>Back to Top</center>

public servants. Note 2:	This duty continues after the person stops being an officer or employee of the Commonwealth authority. Note 3:	This subsection is a civil penalty provision (see Schedule 2).  

</dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>A person who is involved in a contravention of subsection (1) contravenes

this subsection.

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note 1:	Section 5 defines _involved_. Note 2:	This subsection is a civil penalty provision (see Schedule 2).  </dl></dl>

26  Good faith, use of position and use of information&#151;criminal offences

_Good faithofficers_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An officer of a Commonwealth authority commits an offence if he or she:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>is reckless; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>is intentionally dishonest;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

and fails to exercise his or her powers and discharge his or her duties:

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>in good faith in what he or she believes to be in the best interests of

the Commonwealth authority; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>for a proper purpose.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Section 187 of the Corporations Law deals with the position

of directors of wholly-owned subsidiaries of Commonwealth authorities.

 </dl></dl>

Penalty:	Imprisonment for 5 years.

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>An officer or employee of a Commonwealth authority commits an offence if

he or she uses his or her position dishonestly:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>with the intention of directly or indirectly gaining an advantage for

himself or herself, or someone else, or causing detriment to the Commonwealth

authority or to another person; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>recklessly as to whether the use may result in him or her or someone else

directly or indirectly gaining an advantage, or in causing detriment to the

Commonwealth authority or to another person.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

Penalty:	Imprisonment for 5 years.

_Use of informationofficers and employees_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>A person who obtains information because he or she is, or has been, an

officer or employee of a Commonwealth authority commits an offence if he or she

uses the information dishonestly:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>with the intention of directly or indirectly gaining an advantage for

himself or herself, or someone else, or causing detriment to the Commonwealth

authority or to another person; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>recklessly as to whether the use may result in himself or herself or

someone else directly or indirectly gaining an advantage, or in causing

detriment to the Commonwealth authority or to another person.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

Maximum penalty:	Imprisonment for 5 years.

27A  Compliance with statutory duties

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>An officer does not contravene section 23, 24 or 25, or commit an offence

against section 26, by doing an act that another provision of this Act requires

the officer to do.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>If an officer of a Commonwealth authority is also a public servant, the officer does not contravene section 23, 24 or 25, or commit an offence against 
<center>Back to Top</center>
 section 26, by doing an act in the course of the performance of his or her duties as a public servant. For this purpose, _public servant_ means an a person appointed or engaged under the _Public Service Act 1999_. 

</dd> </dl>

27B  Interaction of sections 22 to 26 with other laws etc.

<dl compact="">

		Sections 22 to 26:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>have effect in addition to, and not in derogation of, any rule of law

relating to the duty or liability of a person because of his or her office or

employment in relation to a Commonwealth authority; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>do not prevent the commencement of proceedings for a breach of duty or in

respect of a liability referred to in paragraph (a).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

This section does not apply to subsections 22(2) and (3) to the extent to which they operate on the duties at common law and in equity that are equivalent to the requirements of subsection 22(1).

27C  Disqualification order for contravention of civil penalty provision

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The Court may disqualify a person from managing bodies corporate for a

period that the Court considers appropriate if:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a declaration is made under clause 1 of Schedule 2 (civil penalty

provision) that the person has contravened a civil penalty provision; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the Court is satisfied that the disqualification is justified.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>An application for a disqualification order under subsection (1) may be

made by:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the Finance Minister; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>some other person authorised in writing by the Finance Minister, under

this paragraph, to make the application.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

An authorisation for the purposes of paragraph (b) may relate to applications in relation to specified contraventions, or to all contraventions, of civil penalty provisions.

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>In determining whether the disqualification is justified, the Court may

have regard to:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the person's conduct in relation to the management, business or property

of any Commonwealth authority or other body corporate; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>any other matters that the Court considers appropriate.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>If a disqualification order under subsection (1) is in force against a

person, the person must not be a director of a Commonwealth authority except

with the leave of the Court.

</dd> </dl>

Maximum penalty: 	Imprisonment for 1 year.

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>When granting leave under subsection (4), the Court may impose conditions

or restrictions that the Court considers appropriate.</dd> <dt>(6)</dt><dd>A person must not contravene a condition or restriction imposed under subsection (5). </dd> </dl>

Maximum penalty:	Imprisonment for 1 year.

<dl compact="">

<dt>(7)</dt><dd>A person may only apply for leave under subsection (4) if he or she has

given the Finance Minister at least 21 days notice of the application.</dd> <dt>(8)</dt><dd>On the application of the Finance Minister, the Court may revoke leave granted under subsection (4). </dd> 
<center>Back to Top</center>

</dl>

27D  Reliance on information or advice provided by others

<dl compact="">

		If:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a director relies on information, or professional or expert advice, given

or prepared by:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>an employee of the Commonwealth authority whom the director believes on

reasonable grounds to be reliable and competent in relation to the matters

concerned; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>a professional adviser or expert in relation to matters that the director

believes on reasonable grounds to be within the person's professional or expert

competence; or</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>another director or officer in relation to matters within the director's

or officer's authority; or</dd>

<dt>(iv)</dt><dd>a committee of directors on which the director did not serve in relation

to matters within the committee's authority; and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the reliance was made:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>in good faith; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>after making proper inquiry if the circumstances indicated the need for

inquiry; and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the reasonableness of the director's reliance on the information or advice

arises in proceedings brought to determine whether a director has performed a

duty under this Division or an equivalent general law duty;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

the director's reliance on the information or advice is taken to be reasonable unless the contrary is proved.

27E  Responsibility for actions of delegate

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>If the directors of a Commonwealth authority delegate a power under its

enabling legislation, a director is responsible for the exercise of the power

by the delegate as if the power had been exercised by the directors

themselves.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>A director is not responsible under subsection (1) if: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the director believed on reasonable grounds at all times that the delegate

would exercise the power in conformity with the duties imposed on directors of

the Commonwealth authority by this Act and the authority's enabling

legislation; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the director believed:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>on reasonable grounds; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>in good faith; and</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>after making proper inquiry if the circumstances indicated the need for

inquiry;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		that the delegate was reliable and competent in relation to the power

delegated.

</dl></dl></dl>

Subdivision B&#151;Disclosure of, and voting on matters involving, material personal interests
 27F  Material personal interest&#151;director's duty to disclose

_Director&apos;s duty to notify other directors of material personal interest when conflict arises_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A director of a Commonwealth authority who has a material personal

interest in a matter that relates to the affairs of the authority must give the

other directors notice of the interest unless subsection (2) says otherwise.</dd> 
<center>Back to Top</center>
 <dt>(2)</dt><dd>The director does not need to give notice of an interest under subsection <dt>(1)</dt><dd>if: </dd>

</dd>

</dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the interest:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>arises in relation to the director's remuneration as a director of the

authority; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>relates to a contract that insures, or would insure, the director against

liabilities the director incurs as an officer of the authority (but only if the

contract does not make the authority or a subsidiary of the authority the

insurer); or</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>relates to any payment by the authority or a subsidiary of the authority

in respect of an indemnity permitted under section 27M or any contract relating

to such an indemnity; or</dd>

<dt>(iv)</dt><dd>is in a contract, or proposed contract, with, or for the benefit of, or

on behalf of, a subsidiary of the authority and arises merely because the

director is a director of the subsidiary; or

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>all the following conditions are satisfied:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the director has already given notice of the nature and extent of the

interest and its relation to the affairs of the authority under subsection

(1)</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>if a person who was not a director of the authority at the time when the

notice under subsection (1) was given is appointed as a director of the

authority&#151;the notice is given to that person</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>the nature or extent of the interest has not materially increased above

that disclosed in the notice; or

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the director has given a standing notice of the nature and extent of the

interest under section 27G and the notice is still effective in relation to the

interest.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>The notice required by subsection (1) must:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>give details of:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the nature and extent of the interest; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>the relation of the interest to the affairs of the authority; and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>be given at a directors' meeting as soon as practicable after the director

becomes aware of his or her interest in the matter.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

The details must be recorded in the minutes of the meeting.

_Effect of contravention by director_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>A contravention of this section by a director does not affect the validity

of any act, transaction, agreement, instrument, resolution or other thing.

</dd> </dl>

27G  Director may give other directors standing notice about an interest

_Power to give notice_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A director of a Commonwealth authority who has an interest in a matter may

give the other directors standing notice of the nature and extent of the

interest in the matter in accordance with subsection (2). The notice may be

given at any time and whether or not the matter relates to the affairs of the

authority at the time the notice is given.

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

Note:	The standing notice may be given to the other directors

before the interest becomes a material personal interest.

</dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The notice under subsection (1) must:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>give details of the nature and extent of the interest; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>be given:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>at a directors' meeting (either orally or in writing); or </dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>to the other directors individually in writing.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

The standing notice is given under subparagraph (b)(ii) when it has been given to every director.

_Standing notice must be tabled at meeting if given to directors individually_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>If the standing notice is given to the other directors individually in

writing it must be tabled at the next directors' meeting after it is given.

</dd> </dl>

_Nature and extent of interest must be recorded in minutes_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>The director must ensure that the nature and extent of the interest

disclosed in the standing notice is recorded in the minutes of the meeting at

which the standing notice is given or tabled.

</dd> </dl>

_Dates of effect and expiry of standing notice_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>The standing notice:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>takes effect as soon as it is given; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>ceases to have effect if a person who was not a director of the authority

at the time when the notice was given is appointed as a director of the

authority.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

A standing notice that ceases to have effect under paragraph (b) commences to have effect again if it is given to the person referred to in that paragraph.

_Effect of material increase in nature or extent of interest_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(6)</dt><dd>The standing notice ceases to have effect in relation to a particular

interest if the nature or extent of the interest materially increases above

that disclosed in the notice.

</dd> </dl>

_Effect of contravention by director_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(7)</dt><dd>A contravention of this section by a director does not affect the validity

of any act, transaction, agreement, instrument, resolution or other thing.

</dd> </dl>

27H  Interaction of sections 27F and 27G with other laws etc.

<dl compact="">

		Sections 27F and 27G have effect in addition to, and not in derogation of:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>any general law rule about conflicts of interest; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>any provision in the Commonwealth authority's enabling legislation that

restricts a director from:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>having a material personal interest in a matter; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>holding an office or possessing property;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		involving duties or interests that conflict with their duties or interests as

<center>Back to Top</center>

a director.

</dl></dl></dl>

27J  Restrictions on voting

_Restrictions on voting and being present_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A director of a Commonwealth authority who has a material personal

interest in a matter that is being considered at a directors' meeting must not:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>be present while the matter is being considered at the meeting; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>vote on the matter;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

unless:

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>subsection (2) or (3) allows the director to be present; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>the interest does not need to be disclosed under section 27F.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Participation with approval of other directors_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The director may be present and vote if directors who do not have a

material personal interest in the matter have passed a resolution that:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>identifies the director, the nature and extent of the director's interest

in the matter and its relation to the affairs of the authority; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>states that those directors are satisfied that the interest should not

disqualify the director from voting or being present.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Participation with Ministerial approval_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>The director may be present and vote if they are so entitled under a

declaration or order made by the responsible Minister under section 27K.

</dd> </dl>

_Effect of contravention by director_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>A contravention by a director of:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>this section; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a condition attached to a declaration or order made by the responsible

Minister under section 27K;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

does not affect the validity of any resolution.

27K  Minister's power to make declarations and class orders

_Minister&apos;s power to make specific declarations_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The responsible Minister may declare in writing that a director of a

Commonwealth authority who has a material personal interest in a matter that is

being, or is to be, considered at a directors' meeting may, despite the

director's interest, be present while the matter is being considered at the

meeting, vote on the matter, or both be present and vote. However, the Minister

may only make the declaration if:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the number of directors entitled to be present and vote on the matter

would be less than the quorum for a directors' meeting if the director were not

allowed to vote on the matter at the meeting; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the matter needs to be dealt with urgently, or if there is some other

compelling reason for the matter being dealt with at the directors' meeting.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The declaration may:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>apply to all or only some of the directors; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>specify conditions that the authority or director must comply with.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Responsible Minister&apos;s power to make class orders_

<dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>The responsible Minister may make an order in writing that enables

directors who have a material personal interest in a matter to be present while

the matter is being considered at a directors' meeting, vote on that matter, or

both be present and vote. The order may be made in respect of a specified class

of Commonwealth authorities, directors, resolutions or interests.</dd> <dt>(4)</dt><dd>The order may be expressed to be subject to conditions.</dd> <dt>(5)</dt><dd>Notice of the making, revocation or suspension of the order must be published in the _Gazette_. </dd> 

</dl>

27L  Right of access to authority's books

_Right while director_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A director of a Commonwealth authority may inspect the books of the

authority at all reasonable times for the purposes of a legal proceeding:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>to which the director is a party; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>that the director proposes in good faith to bring; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>that the director has reason to believe will be brought against him or her.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

_Right during 7 years after ceasing to be director_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>A person who has ceased to be a director of a Commonwealth authority may

inspect the books of the authority at all reasonable times for the purposes of

a legal proceeding:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>to which the person is a party; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>that the person proposes in good faith to bring; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>that the person has reason to believe will be brought against him or her.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

This right continues for 7 years after the person ceased to be a director of the authority.

_Right to take copies_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>A person authorised to inspect books under this section for the purposes

of a legal proceeding may make copies of the books for the purposes of those

proceedings.

</dd> </dl>

_Commonwealth authority not to refuse access_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>A Commonwealth authority must allow a person to exercise his or her rights

to inspect or take copies of the books under this section.

</dd> </dl>

Division 4A&#151;Restrictions on indemnities and insurance for officers
 27M  Indemnification and exemption of officer

_Power to indemnify officers_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>Except as provided in this section, a Commonwealth authority may indemnify

a person who is or has been an officer of the authority from any liability

incurred by the person as an officer of the authority.

</dd> </dl>

_Exemptions not allowed_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>A Commonwealth authority, or a subsidiary of a Commonwealth authority,

must not exempt a person (whether directly or through an interposed entity)

from a liability to the authority incurred as an officer of the authority.

</dd> </dl>

_When indemnity for liability (other than for legal costs) not allowed_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>A Commonwealth authority, or a subsidiary of a Commonwealth authority,

must not indemnify a person (whether by agreement or by making a payment and

whether directly or through an interposed entity) against any of the following

liabilities incurred as an officer of the authority:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a liability owed to the authority or a subsidiary of the authority; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a liability for a civil penalty order under clause 3 of Schedule 2 or a

<center>Back to Top</center>

compensation order under clause 4 of Schedule 2; or

</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>a liability that is owed to someone other than the authority or a

subsidiary of the authority and did not arise out of conduct in good faith.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

This subsection does not apply to a liability for legal costs.

_When indemnity for legal costs not allowed_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>A Commonwealth authority, or a subsidiary of a Commonwealth authority,

must not indemnify a person (whether by agreement or by making a payment and

whether directly or through an interposed entity) against legal costs incurred

in defending an action for a liability incurred as an officer of the authority

if the costs are incurred:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>in defending or resisting a proceedings in which the person is found to

have a liability for which they could not be indemnified under subsection (3);

or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>in defending or resisting criminal proceedings in which the person is

found guilty; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>in defending or resisting proceedings brought by the Finance Minister for

a court order if the grounds for making the order are found by the court to

have been established; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>in connection with proceedings for relief to the person under this Act in

which the Court denies the relief.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

Paragraph (c) does not apply to costs incurred in responding to actions taken by the Finance Minister as part of an investigation before commencing proceedings for the court order.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Paragraph (c)&#151;This includes proceedings by the Finance

Minister for an order under section 27C (disqualification order) or clause 3 or

4 of Schedule 2 (civil penalties).

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>For the purposes of subsection (4), the outcome of proceedings is the

outcome of the proceedings and any appeal in relation to the proceedings.

</dd> </dl>

27N  Insurance for certain liabilities of officers

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>Except as provided in subsection (2), a Commonwealth authority may insure

a person who is or has been an officer against liabilities incurred by the

person as an officer.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>A Commonwealth authority, or a subsidiary of a Commonwealth authority, must not pay, or agree to pay, a premium for a contract insuring a person who is, or has been, an officer of the authority against a liability (other than one for legal costs) arising out of: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>conduct involving a wilful breach of duty in relation to the authority;

or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a contravention of section 24 or 25.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

This section applies to a premium whether it is paid directly or through an interposed entity.

27P  Certain indemnities, exemptions, payments and agreements not authorised and certain documents void

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>Sections 27M and 27N do not authorise anything that would otherwise be

unlawful.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>Anything that purports to indemnify or insure a person against a liability or exempt them from a liability is void to the extent that it contravenes section 27M or 27N. </dd> </dl>

12  Schedule 2

Repeal the Schedule, substitute: 

Schedule 2&#151;Civil consequences of contravening civil penalty provisions

 Note:	See section 6.

1  Declarations of contravention

<dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>If a Court is satisfied that a person has contravened 1 of the following

provisions, it must make a declaration of contravention:

</dd> 

</dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>subsections 22(1) and 23(1) and (2), 24(1) and (2), 25(1) and (2)

(officers' duties)</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>subsection 11(1) (annual reporting rules)

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

These provisions are the _civil penalty provisions_.

<dl compact=""><dl compact="">

Note:	Once a declaration has been made, the Finance Minister can

then seek a pecuniary penalty order (clause 3) or a disqualification order

(section 27C).

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>A declaration of contravention must specify the following:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the Court that made the declaration;</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the civil penalty provision that was contravened;</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>the person who contravened the provision;</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>the conduct that constituted the contravention;</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>the Commonwealth authority to which the conduct related.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

2  Declaration of contravention is conclusive evidence

<dl compact="">

		A declaration of contravention is conclusive evidence of the matters referred

to in subclause 1(2).

 </dl>

3  Pecuniary penalty orders

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A Court may order a person to pay the Commonwealth a pecuniary penalty of

up to $200,000 if:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a declaration of contravention by the person has been made under clause 1;

and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the contravention:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>materially prejudices the interests of the Commonwealth authority; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>materially prejudices the Commonwealth authority's ability to pay its

creditors; or</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>is serious.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The penalty is a civil debt payable to the Commonwealth. The Commonwealth

may enforce the order as if it were an order made in civil proceedings against

the person to recover a debt due by the person. The debt arising from the order

is taken to be a judgment debt.

</dd> </dl>

4  Compensation orders

_Compensation for damage suffered_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A Court may order a person to compensate a Commonwealth authority for

damage suffered by the authority if:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the person has contravened a civil penalty provision in relation to the

authority; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the damage resulted from the contravention.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

The order must specify the amount of the compensation.

<dl compact="">

		_Damage includes profits_ <dt>(2)</dt><dd>In determining the damage suffered by the Commonwealth authority for the purposes of making a compensation order, include profits made by any person resulting from the contravention or the offence.</dd> 
<center>Back to Top</center>
 		_Recovery of damage_ <dt>(3)</dt><dd>A compensation order may be enforced as if it were a judgment of the Court. </dd> 

</dl>

5  Effect of clause 4

<dl compact="">

		Clause 4:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>has effect in addition to, and not in derogation of, any rule of law about

the duty or liability of a person because of the person's office or employment

in relation to a Commonwealth authority; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>does not prevent proceedings from being instituted in respect of such a

duty or in respect of such a liability.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

6  Who may apply for a declaration or order

_Application by Finance Minister_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The Finance Minister, or some other person authorised in writing by the

Finance Minister under this subclause to make the application, may apply for a

declaration of contravention, a pecuniary penalty order or a compensation order.

</dd> </dl>

_Application by Commonwealth authority_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The Commonwealth authority may apply for a compensation order.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>The Commonwealth authority may intervene in an application for a declaration of contravention or a pecuniary penalty order in relation to the Commonwealth authority. The Commonwealth authority is entitled to be heard on all matters other than whether the declaration or order should be made. </dd> </dl>

_No one else may apply_

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>No person may apply for a declaration of contravention, a pecuniary

penalty order or a compensation order unless permitted by this clause.</dd> <dt>(5)</dt><dd>Subclause (4) does not exclude the operation of the _Director of Public Prosecutions Act 1983_.  </dd> </dl>

7  Time limit for application for a declaration or order

<dl compact="">

		Proceedings for a declaration of contravention, a pecuniary penalty order, or

a compensation order, may be started no later than 6 years after the

contravention.

 </dl>

8  Civil evidence and procedure rules for declarations of contravention and civil penalty orders

<dl compact="">

		The Court must apply the rules of evidence and procedure for civil matters

when hearing proceedings for:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a declaration of contravention; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a pecuniary penalty order.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

9  Civil proceedings after criminal proceedings

<dl compact="">

		A court must not make a declaration of contravention or a pecuniary penalty

order against a person for a contravention if the person has been convicted of

an offence constituted by conduct that is substantially the same as the conduct

constituting the contravention.

 </dl>

10  Criminal proceedings during civil proceedings

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>Proceedings for a declaration of contravention or pecuniary penalty order

against a person are stayed if:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>criminal proceedings are started or have already been started against the

person for an offence; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the offence is constituted by conduct that is substantially the same as

the conduct alleged to  constitute the contravention.

<center>Back to Top</center>

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The proceedings for the declaration or order may be resumed if the person

is not convicted of the offence. Otherwise, the proceedings for the declaration

or order are dismissed.

</dd> </dl>

11  Criminal proceedings after civil proceedings

<dl compact="">

		Criminal proceedings may be started against a person for conduct that is

substantially the same as conduct constituting a contravention of a civil

penalty provision regardless of whether:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a declaration of contravention has been made against the person; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a pecuniary penalty order has been made against the person; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>a compensation order has been made against the person; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>the person has been disqualified from managing a Commonwealth authority

under section 27C.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

12  Evidence given in proceedings for penalty not admissible in criminal proceedings

<dl compact="">

		Evidence of information given or evidence of production of documents by an

individual is not admissible in criminal proceedings against the individual if:

 </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>the individual previously gave the evidence or produced the documents in

proceedings for a pecuniary penalty order against the individual for a

contravention of a civil penalty provision (whether or not the order was made);

and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the conduct alleged to constitute the offence is substantially the same as

the conduct that was claimed to constitute the contravention.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

However, this does not apply to a criminal proceeding in respect of the falsity of the evidence given by the individual in the proceedings for the pecuniary penalty order.

13  Finance Minister requiring person to assist

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>The Finance Minister may require a person to give all reasonable

assistance in connection with:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>an application for a declaration of contravention or a pecuniary penalty

order; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>criminal proceedings for an offence against this Act.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

The person must comply with the request.

Maximum penalty:	5 penalty units.

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>The Finance Minister can require the person to assist in connection with

an application for a declaration or order if, and only if:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>it appears to the Finance Minister that someone other than the person

required to assist may have contravened a civil penalty provision; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the Finance Minister suspects or believes that the person required to

assist can give information relevant to the application.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>The Finance Minister can require the person to assist in connection with

criminal proceedings if, and only if:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>it appears to the Finance Minister that the person required to assist is

unlikely to be a defendant in the proceedings; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the person required to assist is, in relation to a person who is or should

be a defendant in the proceedings:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>an employee or agent (including a banker or auditor) of the other person;

or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>if the other person is a Commonwealth authority&#151;an officer of the other

person; or</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>if the other person is an individual&#151;a partner of the other person.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(4)</dt><dd>The Finance Minister can require the person to assist regardless of

whether:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>an application for the declaration or penalty order has actually been

made; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>criminal proceedings for the offence have actually begun.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5)</dt><dd>The person cannot be required to assist if they are or have been a lawyer

for:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>in an application for a declaration or penalty order&#151;the person suspected

of the contravention; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>in criminal proceedings&#151;a defendant or likely defendant in the

proceedings.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(6)</dt><dd>The requirement to assist must be given in writing.</dd> <dt>(7)</dt><dd>The Court may order the person to comply with the requirement in a specified way. Only the Finance Minister may apply to the Court for an order under this subsection _._ </dd> </dl>

14  Relief from liability for contravention of civil penalty provision 

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>In this section:

</dd> </dl>

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_eligible proceedings_:

 </dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>means proceedings for a contravention of a civil penalty provision

(including proceedings under clause 4); and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>does not include proceedings for an offence (except so far as the

proceedings relate to the question whether the court should make an order under

clause 4).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>If:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>eligible proceedings are brought against a person; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>in the proceedings it appears to the court that the person has, or may

have, contravened a civil penalty provision but that:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the person has acted honestly; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>having regard to all the circumstances of the case, the person ought

fairly to be excused for the contravention;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

the court may relieve the person either wholly or partly from a liability to which the person would otherwise be subject, or that might otherwise be imposed on the person, because of the contravention.

<dl compact="">

<dt>(3)</dt><dd>If a person thinks that eligible proceedings will or may be begun against

them, they may apply to the Court for relief.</dd> <dt>(4)</dt><dd>On an application under subclause (3), the Court may grant relief under subclause (2) as if the eligible proceedings had been begun in the Court.</dd> <dt>(5)</dt><dd>For the purposes of subclause (2) as applying for the purposes of a case 
<center>Back to Top</center>
 tried by a judge with a jury: 

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a reference in that subclause to the court is a reference to the judge;

and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the relief that may be granted includes withdrawing the case in whole or

in part from the jury and directing judgment to be entered for the defendant on

such terms as to costs as the judge thinks appropriate.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

15  Power to grant relief

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>If:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>civil proceedings are brought against an officer of a Commonwealth

authority for negligence, default, breach of trust or breach of duty in a

capacity as such an officer; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>in the proceedings it appears to the court before which the proceedings

are taken that:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the officer is or may be liable in respect of the negligence, default or

breach; and</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>the officer has acted honestly; and</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>having regard to all the circumstances of the case (including those

connected with the officer's appointment), the officer ought fairly to be

excused for the negligence, default or breach;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

the court may relieve the officer either wholly or partly from liability on the terms that the court thinks appropriate.

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>An officer of a Commonwealth authority who has reason to apprehend that a

claim will or might be made against him or her for negligence, default, breach

of trust or breach of duty in a capacity as such an officer may apply to the

Court for relief. On the application, the Court has the same power to relieve

the officer as it would have had under subclause (1) if it had been a court

before which proceedings against the officer for negligence, default, breach of

trust or breach of duty had been brought.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>If: </dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a case to which subclause (1) applies is being tried by a judge with a

jury; and</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>the judge after hearing the evidence is satisfied that the defendant ought

pursuant to that subclause to be relieved either wholly or partly from the

liability sought to be enforced against the officer;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

the judge may withdraw the case in whole or in part from the jury and forthwith direct judgment to be entered for the defendant on the terms as to costs or otherwise that the judge thinks proper. 

Schedule 3&#151;Application, transitional and savings provisions

1  Meaning of commencement, new Law and old Law

<dl compact="">

		In this Schedule:

 </dl>

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_commencement_ means the commencement of the _Corporate Law Economic Reform Program Act 1999_. _new Law_ means this Act as in force after commencement. _old Law_ means this Act as in force immediately before commencement.  </dl></dl>

2  References to provisions of old Law in laws and other documents

<dl compact="">

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A reference in any law of the Commonwealth or of a State or Territory, or

in any document, to a provision of the old Law is to be read after commencement

as a reference to the corresponding provision of the new Law except so far as

the contrary intention appears in the law or document.</dd> 
<center>Back to Top</center>
 <dt>(2)</dt><dd>Without limiting subclause (1), sections 27F to 27K of the new Law correspond to section 21 of the old Law. </dd> 

</dl>

have arisen, on or before commencement. Column 3 sets out how the things and

situations will be dealt with after commencement&#151;either under the old Law or

the new Law.

<dl compact="">

</dd> </dl>

despite its repeal.

<dl compact="">

immediately before commencement continues to have effect after commencement as

if it were made under section 27C of the new Law.</dd> <dt>(2)</dt><dd>An order in force under paragraph 4(b) of Schedule 2 to the old Law immediately before commencement continues to have effect after commencement as if it were made under clause 3 of Schedule 2 to the new Law. </dd> </dl>

10 After subsection 252N(2)

Insert:

<dl compact="">

12  Section 123

Repeal the section, substitute:

123  Members to disclose certain interests to Minister

<dl compact="">

<center>Back to Top</center>

<dt>(1)</dt><dd>A member must, in accordance with this section, disclose to the Minister:

</dd> 

</dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>any direct or indirect pecuniary interest that the member has or acquires

in:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>a body corporate carrying on business in Australia; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>a business in Australia; and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>any direct or indirect pecuniary interest that the member has or acquires

in interests (including securities, futures contracts or other financial

products) regulated by the Commission; and</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>any agreement, understanding or expectation that the member will:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>resume a previous business relationship (whether or not that relationship

existed immediately before the member's appointment); or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>enter into a new business relationship;

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

		when the member ceases to be a member; and

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>any severance arrangement or ongoing financial arrangement that takes

account of an agreement, understanding or expectation that must be disclosed

under paragraph (c).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(2)</dt><dd>For the purpose of paragraph (1)(b), interests are regulated by the

Commission if the Commission has a function or power in relation to any aspect

of the acquisition, holding, disposal or provision of the interests, or of

interests of that kind.</dd> <dt>(3)</dt><dd>In disclosing an indirect pecuniary interest in securities, futures contracts or other financial products, the member must identify the particular securities, futures contracts or products.</dd> <dt>(4)</dt><dd>Paragraphs (1)(c) and (d) apply to agreements or understandings entered into, or expectations arising, before or after the member's appointment.</dd> <dt>(5)</dt><dd>Paragraph (1)(c) does not require a member to disclose an expectation to enter into a new business relationship unless the member can identify the other party, or one or more other parties, to the relationship. Disclosure is required whether or not the field of business or legal nature of the relationship has been determined.</dd> <dt>(6)</dt><dd>A disclosure under this section must be made in writing. </dd> </dl>

13  Paragraph 124(1)(b)

Omit "or other interest", substitute "interest, or a direct or indirect interest of any other kind,".

17  After subsection 243D(5)

Insert:

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5A)</dt><dd>If a cash dealer communicates to the Director, under subsection (1),

information about the cash dealer's suspicion in relation to a transaction to

which the cash dealer is a party, the cash dealer must not, unless required to

do so under the ASC Law, the Corporations Law or an Act of the Commonwealth,

disclose to anyone else:

<center>Back to Top</center>

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>that the cash dealer has formed the suspicion; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>that information has been communicated to the Director; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>any other information from which the person to whom the information is

disclosed could reasonably be expected to infer that:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>the suspicion had been formed; or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>the first-mentioned information had been communicated.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5B)</dt><dd>If a cash dealer gives further information pursuant to a request under

subsection (4), the cash dealer must not, unless required to do so under the

ASC Law or an Act of the Commonwealth, disclose to anyone else:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>that the information has been given; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>any other information from which the person to whom the information is

disclosed could reasonably be expected to infer that the first-mentioned

information had been given.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5C)</dt><dd>A cash dealer who contravenes subsection (5A) or (5B) is guilty of an

offence punishable, upon conviction, by:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>a fine of not more than 120 penalty units or imprisonment for not more

than 2 years, or both, if the cash dealer is a natural person; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>a fine of not more than 600 penalty units if the cash dealer is a body

corporate.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5D)</dt><dd>Neither subsection (5A) nor subsection (5B) prohibits a cash dealer from

communicating or disclosing a fact or information referred to in either of

those subsections:

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>to the Australian Stock Exchange Limited; or</dd>

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>to the Commission; or</dd>

<dt>(c)</dt><dd>to a body corporate approved under section 769 of the Corporations Law as

a stock exchange; or</dd>

<dt>(d)</dt><dd>to a body corporate approved under section 770 of the Corporations Law as

an approved securities organisation; or</dd>

<dt>(e)</dt><dd>in accordance with conditions imposed by the Minister when approving under

section 770A of the Corporations Law a stock market for electronic trading of

interests in a registered scheme; or</dd>

<dt>(f)</dt><dd>in accordance with conditions imposed by the Minister when declaring a

specified stock market to be an exempt stock market under section 771 of the

Corporations Law; or</dd>

<dt>(g)</dt><dd>to a body corporate approved under section 779B of the Corporations Law as

a securities clearing house; or</dd>

<dt>(h)</dt><dd>to a body corporate approved under section 1126 of the Corporations Law as

a futures exchange; or</dd>

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>in accordance with conditions imposed by the Minister when declaring a

specified futures market to be an exempt futures market under section 1127 of

the Corporations Law; or</dd>

<dt>(j)</dt><dd>to a body corporate approved under section 1131 of the Corporations Law as

a clearing house for a futures exchange; or</dd>

<dt>(k)</dt><dd>to a body corporate approved under section 1132 of the Corporations Law as

a futures association.

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5E)</dt><dd>Neither subsection (5A) nor subsection (5B) prohibits a cash dealer from

communicating or disclosing to any court any information, or matter, referred

to in that subsection, but this subsection does not affect the operation of

subsection (5F).</dd> <dt>(5F)</dt><dd>In any legal proceeding (other than a prosecution for an offence against subsection 29(1) or 30(1) of the _Financial Transaction Reports Act 1988_(which relate to false and misleading information or incomplete information) as applied by subsection (7) of this section): 
<center>Back to Top</center>

</dd> </dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(a)</dt><dd>none of the following is admissible in evidence:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>a report prepared (whether before or after the commencement of this

subsection) under subsection (1);</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>a copy of such a report;</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>a document purporting to set out information contained in such a

report;</dd>

<dt>(iv)</dt><dd>a document given under subsection (4); and

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(b)</dt><dd>evidence is not admissible as to:

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

<dt>(i)</dt><dd>whether or not a report was prepared under subsection (1); or</dd>

<dt>(ii)</dt><dd>whether or not a copy of a report prepared under that subsection, or a

document purporting to set out information contained in such a report, was

given to, or received by, the Director; or</dd>

<dt>(iii)</dt><dd>whether or not particular information was contained in a report prepared

under that subsection; or</dd>

<dt>(iv)</dt><dd>whether or not particular information was given under subsection (4).

</dd>

</dl></dl></dl></dl>

<dl compact="">

<dt>(5G)</dt><dd>In subsection (5F):

</dd> </dl>

<def><dl compact=""><dl compact="">

_information_ includes the formation or existence of a suspicion

referred to in subsection (1).

 </dl></dl>
